ZHANG QUN ARRIVES IN BEIPING ON JIANG'S ORDERS

To Confer with Zhang Xueliang on Important Matters

Beiping dispatch: Zhang Qun recently came north to Beiping on orders from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. He left Hankou on the 11th, first going to Kaifeng to represent Chiang in offering condolences for the passing of Liu Zhi's mother. On the 13th, he passed through Zhengzhou from Bian, taking the Pinghan express train north. He arrived in Beiping at 7:40 AM on the 14th. Wan Fulin, Wang Shuhan, Tang Guozhen, and Jiang Bocheng, among others, all went to the West Station to greet him. After Zhang alighted from the train, he took a car to his residence at the Beijing Hotel to rest. Wang and Jiang accompanied him to the hotel and met with him for a long time. Wan Fulin hosted a banquet at his residence at 7:00 PM that evening to welcome Zhang, and invited important military and political figures from Beiping to attend. Zhang also scheduled to visit Director of Pacification Zhang Xueliang that evening to confer on important matters. According to Zhang, "This time I have come to Beiping to visit Director Zhang and have no special mission. The length of my stay in Beiping has not been determined. Since I haven't been to the north in over a year, I plan to stay for a few more days. My departure from Beiping may not be via the Pinghan Railway southward; I may first go to Tianjin and then take the Jinpu Railway to Nanjing and then to Hankou. Regarding the suppression of bandits in the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, before Commander-in-Chief Chiang went to Hankou, the provinces had joint defense, but there was a lack of command convenience, so there were no satisfactory results. Commander-in-Chief Chiang came to Hankou to take overall control for thorough elimination. There should be concrete measures for the suppression plan. The Sichuan troops under Fan Shaozeng in western Hubei previously came into contact with bandits in the Songzi area and suffered slight damage. Currently, they have achieved victory. The communist bandits in Macheng, eastern Hubei, are currently confronting government troops outside the city and have not attacked the city. Now that the bandits have heard of the advance of a large army, they plan to flee into mountain lairs and are being pursued by government troops; defeat is imminent and not a problem. The situation of bandit suppression in Anhui Province is also progressing. The communist bandits in the southern section of the Henan Pinghan Railway have been defeated. The defenses in southern Henan, where Ma Hongkui, Liu Zhi, and Zhang Fang are stationed, are solid, and the communist bandits are no longer able to rise up again. When I passed through Wusheng Pass, I met Ma Hongkui. He said that the bandit problem in southern Henan would soon be completely eliminated, etc. Also, the headquarters of the communist bandits in the three provinces is in the mountains of Shangcheng County, Henan. The strategy adopted by the communist bandits is to avoid strength and attack weakness, dividing into smaller units. The headquarters has strict measures to deal with this and anticipates that the communist bandits in the three provinces can be eliminated within two or three months. Commander-in-Chief Chiang will not leave Hankou for the time being; whether he will go to Hunan has not been determined. The rumor that the troops stationed in North China will be transferred south to assist in bandit suppression is not accurate. The small portion previously transferred was to suppress the bandit troops of Liu Guitang and is unrelated to this matter. This time, the bandit suppression in the three provinces does not focus solely on suppression. Among the communist bandits, there are many who joined due to intimidation and coercion, so it was decided to implement both pacification and suppression. The Party and Government Committee in the bandit areas was established based on this practical need and also to handle post-bandit affairs. Initially, it was intended to establish a Political Bureau, but it was later decided to expand its scope and change it to a Party and Government Committee because (1) the Bureau could only be managed by the Director and not a committee system, and (2) Party affairs should not be included. This committee is directly under the Bandit Suppression Headquarters of the three provinces and has supervisory and guiding functions but is not external. The members of the committee do not hold local government positions so that they can focus on the pacification of bandit areas and post-disaster work. Each of the three provinces has a Party and Government Conference; the members of the local government and Party headquarters are all ex officio members and belong to the Party and Government Committee, whose nature is the same as the Party and Government Committee. All matters concerning post-bandit affairs reported to the headquarters are directly presented to the Party and Government Committee for forwarding and processing. The regulations of the Party and Government Committee were agreed upon before I left Hankou and have now been announced and established. The detailed organization need not be repeated. The duties of the Political Affairs Guidance Office that I am in charge of will be handled by the Deputy Director during my absence." Finally, when discussing diplomatic issues, the reporter first asked if China had any intention of turning the Northeast into an autonomous region, as reported by the Japanese side to the League of Nations investigation team. According to the response, "I have not heard of this matter and believe that it is absolutely impossible. Regarding the current diplomatic situation, the following conclusion can be drawn: Today's diplomacy allows neither optimism nor pessimism. The whole country should unite and work together with a spirit of great fearlessness and effective methods to carry out everything. There is hope for the future," etc. (15th)

SONG QINGLING ET AL. GUARANTEE BAW DINH'S RELEASE AGAIN

Baw Dinh and his wife sent to the mausoleum for treatment

Song Qingling, Cai Yuanpei, Yang Xingfo, and others previously sent a letter guaranteeing the release of Baw Dinh and his wife to Shanghai for medical treatment, and then sent another letter requesting the withdrawal of the guarantee. On the 16th, Yang Xingfo came to Nanjing again to request the guarantee again. Song Qingling also arrived in Nanjing on the morning of the 17th to proceed together. After several rounds of negotiation, Baw Dinh and his wife were finally transferred to the vicinity of Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum for treatment at 7:30 PM on the 17th with the approval of the court. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

Song Qingling comes to Nanjing to request guarantee: Song Qingling, Yang Xingfo, etc., upon learning that the resignations of Law Chief Luo Wengan and Vice Minister Zheng Tianxi were not due to their request to guarantee the release of Baw Dinh and his wife, decided to request the guarantee again. After Yang Xingfo arrived in Nanjing on the morning of the 16th, he visited Luo Wengan twice. Luo said that the request for temporary guarantee was in accordance with the law, but the court should not interfere with the judiciary through administration, and since he had already resigned, he had no right to intervene. Therefore, he asked Yang and others to contact the Jiangsu High Court, which was hearing the case. On the night of the 16th, Ms. Song Qingling also came to Nanjing from Shanghai by train, arriving at about 7:00 AM on the morning of the 17th. After getting off the train, she immediately went with Yang Xingfo to the Jiangning District Court Detention Center to visit Baw Dinh and his wife, informing them of the intention to request the guarantee again and offering words of comfort. Song, Yang, and others then left the court to visit Luo Wengan, but Luo was dealing with important official business before leaving for elsewhere and did not meet them. At 11:00 AM, Song, Yang, and Feng Jiesi, a relative of Baw Dinh and his wife, went to the Jiangning District Court together. Li, the Director of the Ministry of Justice and Administration, also arrived at the time, and they immediately discussed the guarantee procedures in the reception room together.

The Court Approves Temporary Release on Bail: When Song, Yang, Li, Feng, and others were discussing in the reception room, they all used English and prohibited others from entering the room. The discussion lasted for an hour and a half, with Yang Xingfo speaking the most, exhausting his request for release responsibility. It was heard that initially, Song, Yang, and others still intended to ask the court to allow them to be transferred to Shanghai for medical treatment, but the court held that the case still needed to be tried continuously before the jurisdiction issue was resolved. If they could not be summoned as needed when the court was in session, it would cause great difficulties for the trial. Moreover, it was unknown whether there would be accidents along the way when Baw Dinh and his wife were transferred to Shanghai, and the guarantor had to bear full responsibility, so it was not approved. Song, Yang, and others also felt that the responsibility was too great, so the result of the discussion was to decide to seek medical treatment in Nanjing. At 12:30 PM, Song, Yang, and others went to Baw Dinh and his wife to inform them of this intention, but Baw Dinh and his wife expressed disagreement. Song, Yang, Li, and others then returned to the reception room to negotiate. It was said that the weather had been hot recently, and it was feared that the hospitals would not be adequate, so it was decided to choose a suitable house near the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum and extend medical treatment every day. When Song, Yang, and Li were negotiating, Li Mian, the Criminal Division Chief of the Jiangsu High Court, had already returned to Nanjing from Suzhou on the night of the 16th, but he avoided seeing guests during the trial period and did not participate in the discussion. However, he expressed agreement with the results of the discussion between Song, Yang, and others, so he approved it.

Baw Dinh and his wife leave the court: After the Jiangsu High Court approved the temporary release on bail, the Jiangning District Court Detention Center immediately prepared all the procedures. At 7:30 PM, the Jiangsu High Court immediately signed the release of Baw Dinh and his wife from the detention center. Baw Dinh and his wife had been on hunger strike for sixteen days and could not walk, so the detention center sent people to carry them out to the car outside the door and drive them to a house near the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum for recuperation. The Jiangsu High Court also sent police to guard them. It was heard that Baw Dinh and his wife had expressed their intention to resume eating immediately after leaving the court and would be properly cared for by doctors, starting with nutritious liquids. It was heard that Song Qingling, Yang Xingfo, and others left Nanjing for Shanghai on the night of the 17th after the procedures were completed.

Comments from legal experts expressing indignation: On the 17th, the reporter met a legal expert in Nanjing and asked for his opinion on the Baw Dinh and his wife hunger strike case. He gave a fair and detailed opinion as follows: "The case of Baw Dinh and his wife endangering the Republic of China is very serious, but the handling procedures are very simple. The court only needs to conduct a trial in accordance with the law, investigate the evidence, and judge whether they have committed a crime or the severity of the crime according to the law. However, Baw Dinh and his wife have consistently refused to be tried, seeking favors and making unreasonable demands, directly despising our country's laws and being enemies of the law. They started a hunger strike because their request to apply for jurisdiction and hire foreign lawyers to defend them was not allowed. While expressing their firm hunger strike, they also accepted the diagnosis and treatment of doctors, making it clear that they had no determination to die and were intimidating and coercing. The court has done its duty by trying its best to guide them and extending medical treatment every day since they went on hunger strike. If Baw Dinh and his wife unfortunately starve to death in prison, it will be their own fault, and the court will not bear the slightest responsibility. Song Qingling, Cai Yuanpei, Yang Xingfo, and others requested the court to temporarily release them on bail, and they insisted that they must be sent to a hospital in Shanghai and refused to receive treatment in a hospital in Nanjing, which is even more unreasonable. The diseases caused by their hunger strike are their own fault. And the hospitals in Nanjing, such as the Central Hospital and Gulou Hospital, are well-equipped and can treat the diseases caused by the hunger strike. Why must they go to a hospital in Shanghai to be treated? It is speculated that their intention is nothing more than to use this to forcefully pressure the court and achieve their goal of transferring jurisdiction and hiring foreign lawyers. The judicial authorities resigned in anger because of this, and this spirit is deeply admired by us. What the judicial authorities are fighting for is to maintain the law. It is a shining example for our country's political circles to abandon their position and fight for the sake of maintaining the law. At a time when our country's judicial politics is in its infancy, it is necessary to maintain its spirit of independence, and extraterritorial rights must be actively recovered. In the future, foreigners who commit crimes must be tried under our country's laws. If we relax the law against a stateless criminal who endangers the Republic of China at this time, then everyone will follow suit in the future, and what law will our country have? The destruction of the judiciary will be unimaginable. Now is a time of national crisis, with internal and external troubles pressing in on us. The way to save our country from danger depends on the efforts and struggles of our people. Whether Baw Dinh and his wife have committed a crime or the severity of the crime can be judged by the court in accordance with the law. There is no need to stir up such a big wave in the Judicial Yuan. If Baw Dinh and his wife are scholars and should be given special consideration, then there are countless scholars and young people in our country who have been convicted of endangering the Republic of China. Lightly treating Chinese and valuing foreigners, what is the reason for this? Moreover, Baw Dinh and his wife still need to be tried in accordance with the law," etc. He was extremely indignant during his speech. (Central News Agency)

FUZHOU MERCHANTS AND RESIDENTS STRIKE

Opposing the Provincial Government's Collection of House and Shop Donations

Fuzhou dispatch: Merchants and residents in Fujian oppose the provincial government's heavy collection of house and shop donations. On the morning of the 14th, the Commercial Affairs Research Institute and Fire Brigade of each shop held a joint meeting and decided to thoroughly oppose it. They also requested the Nineteenth Route Army Commander Cai Tingkai to come to the province as their backing. They notified all shops in the city to post slogans at their doors, uniformly saying "Welcome Nineteenth Route Army Commander Cai Tingkai, we vow to deny the heavy collection of house and shop donations" to show their determination. Unexpectedly, the Municipal Public Security Bureau sent a large number of officers and inspectors that evening to supervise the police to clear the streets, using black paint to paint over the seven characters "deny the heavy collection of house and shop donations," leaving only the eleven characters "Welcome Nineteenth Route Army Commander Cai Tingkai we vow," completely changing the meaning. When the merchants and residents opened their shops on the morning of the 15th and saw that the slogans had been painted over, they were deeply suspicious. Unexpectedly, at 9:00 AM, the House and Shop Donation Office suddenly sent a large number of security police teams and soldiers from the Second Brigade of the Provincial Defense Army, fully armed, to forcibly collect donations in cooperation with the collectors, first in the busiest Nan Street and Zhongting Street shops in the city. Those who resisted were immediately arrested, causing great anger among the shops, which immediately announced a strike. Upon hearing the news, the Commercial Affairs Research Institute of each shop held an emergency meeting at the Shanghang Street County Chamber of Commerce at 10:00 AM, resolving that all shops in the city would strike in resistance. After the meeting, the representatives set off in cars, shouting along the way slogans such as "The government violently extorts house and shop donations, merchants should unanimously strike to resist." All shops in the city closed their doors and raised white cloth flags in front of the shops and on the upper floors, saying "We will not open the market until the house and shop donations are revoked." At 1:00 PM, the Fire Brigade of each shop also held a temporary meeting at the Xiapu Street Fire Brigade Federation, deciding that each brigade should summon support members (about a hundred people per brigade, with a total of thirty-six brigades in the city) to gather in the brigade and prepare to resist if the government forced the merchants to open their shops, so the situation was extremely serious. Unexpectedly, the government's attitude remained tough, and the police chief of the First Police Station, Shi Taizhen, was still sent to lead the police team to advise the merchants on Nan Street to open their shops, and he was surrounded and beaten, suffering serious injuries. The provincial government has ordered temporary martial law, and the turmoil is expanding. The third declaration against the heavy collection of house and shop donations issued by the Fire Brigade and Commercial Affairs Research Institute of each shop on the 15th is recorded below. This time, the Fujian Provincial Government, disregarding its prestige and disregarding the hardships of the people, heavily collected house and shop donations. The representatives of this association have repeatedly represented public opinion, requesting the authorities to withdraw their order, and have telegraphed the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and the fellow villagers associations in Shanghai and Beijing, as well as various dignitaries, calling for them to telegraph the provincial government immediately and cancel the cases. We have been running around and appealing, but there has been no result. Moreover, the government has stated that the Commercial Affairs Research Institute has not been recognized by the government, and the Fire Brigade is a charitable organization and has no qualifications to petition. The Minhou County Chamber of Commerce was instructed to inform us. The Commercial Affairs Research Institute and the Fire Brigade have a very deep relationship with the history of Fuzhou. Moreover, when the provincial government discussed collecting house and shop donations to suppress bandits during the rampant Red bandits two years ago, it sent a letter summoning each association to send representatives to the government to declare that it would only be collected once and would not be repeated. If each association is not sufficient to represent public opinion, then what is the purpose of the government's summons? The contradiction is the worst. Those who have not been recognized are nothing more than because each Commercial Affairs Research Institute has repeatedly represented public opinion and resisted miscellaneous taxes and harsh levies, incurring the anger of the authorities. However, the requests of each representative are purely to cancel this donation and have no other purpose. If one is punished for requesting, then what is the meaning of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's doctrine of people's rights? Recently, the House and Shop Donation Office has been sending people to forcibly collect donations from shops and residences in various places every day, and people in various places have been holding meetings to discuss this. They all believe that the authorities disregard their prestige and disregard the opinions of the people. All our citizens refuse to pay the house and shop donations and vow to die. If there is forced oppression, we can only make a final struggle within the scope of the law. We must achieve the goal of cancellation so that we will not sink into the endless sea of suffering in the future. No matter what, each citizen must have the will to persevere and the thought of not looking back. This association accepts the aforementioned intention, and in addition to continuing to present a request to the authorities for cancellation and re-telegraphing the central government for appeal, it will make another declaration. I hope you will understand. (15th)

XU YUANQUAN SUPERVISES THE GENERAL ATTACK ON HE LONG'S BANDITS

He Chengjun Goes to Shashi to Inspect Defenses

Hankou dispatch: The remnant bandits of He Long's troops, after being fiercely suppressed by the Tenth Army, suffered extremely heavy losses. Now the bandits and the Duan Dechang faction are running around in central Hubei, eking out a living, and are no longer as rampant as they used to be. Xu Yuanquan, the commander of the Tenth Army and the deputy commander of the left route of bandit suppression, asked for instructions on the deployment of troops after Commander-in-Chief Chiang arrived in Hankou. On the 10th, he set off from Hankou with Chief of Staff Miao Songpei and others. On the 13th, he arrived in Yingcheng. In accordance with the original plan, he began the general attack on the 15th. Xu once gathered Xiao Zhichu, the commander of the Forty-fourth Division, Wan Yaohuang, the commander of the Thirteenth Division, Zhang Zhenhan, the commander of the Forty-first Division, Jiang Zuojun, the brigade commander, Liu Peixu, Huang Xin, Xu Jiwu, and Miao Songpei, the chief of staff of the Tenth Army, and others at Yuekou, and Zhu Huaibing, the director of the Department of Civil Affairs, also participated. A general decision was made regarding post-bandit affairs in the bandit areas. First, in cooperation with the county magistrates and local impartial gentry, the restored people's regiments in each county will be sorted out and trained, and household registration, baojia, and the organization of anti-communist volunteer troops will be carried out to enable the people to obtain self-defense as soon as possible. After the meeting, a telegram was sent to the Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters, asking them to transfer orders to the county magistrates who had come to the province to return to their posts on a scheduled basis in order to achieve the effect of military-government cooperation. Yan Zhongmei, the secretary of the army, telegraphed Hankou from Yingcheng on the 15th, saying that the encirclement and suppression of the remnant bandits had been carried out in accordance with the Commander-in-Chief's methods, and it was expected that the remnant bandits could be annihilated in the shortest possible time. It was also said that according to the captured bandit troops, there was panic in the bandit's internal ranks, and ammunition and food were exhausted. In addition to tempting the people to join them with benefits, they also forced them to transport food for supply. Given the situation in the bandit areas, the general attack will surely have results. As for western Hubei, there are also remnant bandits who are causing trouble, and the Sichuan troops under Wang Lingji and Fan Shaozeng have advanced to suppress them. After Qianjiang was recovered, the bandits' power greatly declined. Now Wang has arrived in Shashi and is uniting with the Tenth Army to suppress the remnant bandits. He Chengjun, the Director of Pacification in Hubei and Commander of the Left Route of Bandit Suppression, went to Shashi by plane on the 15th with Zhu Chuanjing, the chief staff officer, Qiu Jia, the representative of the Twenty-first Army stationed in Hankou, Zhu Xiangwen, the section member of the Quartermaster Department of the Third Army, and others to inspect the defenses in western Hubei and to meet with Wang to discuss bandit suppression military affairs. It is said that he will return to Hankou within one or two days. During He's departure, the affairs of the Pacification Office will be handled jointly by Chief of Staff Yang Kuiyi and Office Director Chen Guangzu.

HAN FUJU IS ABOUT TO RETURN TO JINAN

Inspection of Counties in Western Shandong to Be Completed Soon

Jinan dispatch: Han Fuju, the chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, went to the counties in western Shandong to inspect county administration and investigate the people's livelihood. In recent days, he has successively passed through Taian, Yanzhou, Jining, Jiaxiang, and Juye, inspecting various agencies and gathering the people to speak. At noon on the 14th, Han had already left Juye for Heze, arriving in the afternoon, and immediately inspected various agencies and gathered the people to speak. At 7:00 AM on the morning of the 15th, he left Heze for Dingtao, arriving at 10:00 AM. At 12:00 noon, he inspected the county government, and at 2:00 PM, he gathered the people to speak. At 4:00 PM, he departed from Dingtao and arrived in Caoxian at 6:00 PM. At 8:00 PM, he inspected the county government. It is heard that a telegram has been sent to Jinan saying that he will return to Jinan in two days. (15th)

PROGRESS OF RECOVERY IN THE THREE COUNTIES OF JIADING, TAIHANG, AND BAOSHAN

Jiangsu Construction Department Plans a Program

Since the outbreak of the Battle of Shanghai, the towns in the counties of Jiading, Taicang, and Baoshan have been scarred and severely damaged. The Jiangsu Construction Department previously ordered the county heads to supervise the directors of the construction bureaus to investigate the actual damage in the towns under their jurisdiction in detail and submit the proposed repair plans for verification. Director Dong Xiujia also accompanied Provincial Government Chairman Gu Zhutong to Shanghai to personally inspect the actual situation in order to plan the entire program and seek active recovery methods. It is learned that the department has now drafted a construction and recovery program for the three counties and will submit it to the Provincial Government Committee for discussion, seeking to restore the original state as soon as possible.

In addition, the aftermath of the Jiangnan Seawall Changtai Section project is divided into four sections. The Taicang Parade Ground, Daotang Temple, Fangjia Weir Bridge, and Yanglinkou sections have all started construction one after another. The Xuliujing section is scheduled to start construction on the 23rd of this month. The engineering office of this section has a post-disaster engineering office in Liuhe, with Director Qiu Xijue stationed there to supervise and facilitate the progress. (18th)

Shi Ying's Report at the Memorial Week

Rural Economic Panic and Its Remedial Measures

The Central Government's Office in Beijing held Premier's Memorial Week on the morning of the 18th. Those present included Shi Ying, Chen Lifu, Zheng Zhannan, Xie Zuomin, Zhang Daofan, Li Zonghuang, Huang Jichen, Xiao Jishan, Xiao Zhongzhen, Li Ciwen, and over 600 staff members. Chen Lifu presided over the event. Shi Ying gave a report titled "Rural Economic Panic and Its Remedial Measures," which briefly stated: Our country is based on agriculture, with farmers accounting for more than 80% of the total population. Therefore, the rural economy is the foundation of the national economy. However, in recent years, the rural economy has become increasingly panicked. If we do not make every effort to remedy this, the foundation of the national economy will be shaken. Even without foreign enemies, it would be enough to accelerate our demise. Moreover, at this time when the national crisis is becoming more urgent, facing both internal and external pressures, we are in a precarious state. However, there is currently no detailed investigation or statistics regarding the rural economy. Based on my personal observations, the causes of rural economic panic can be roughly divided into the following points: (1) Banditry, (2) Military disturbances, (3) Too many institutions and corrupt officials, (4) Heavy and complicated taxes, (5) Education not adapted to rural life, (6) Natural disasters, (7) Planting opium. In addition, the inability to fully control tariffs, the excessive naivety of farmers' knowledge, and the failure to improve agricultural technology are also causes of rural economic panic. As for agricultural products, the fact that there are too many farmers becoming bandits, soldiers, and idlers, or inconvenient transportation, or lack of capital, leading to reduced production and increased costs, are all closely related to the rural economy. Therefore, organizing credit cooperatives, establishing farmers' loan offices, developing transportation, improving farmers' agricultural knowledge, cultivating farmers' integrity, promoting farmers' self-defense, and implementing tariff protection policies are all essential measures to rescue the rural economy at present. The above are just the major points. As for the details, due to time constraints, I cannot describe them all. I hope everyone will pay attention to the approaching national crisis. While preparing for revenge, we should have a deep understanding of the phenomenon of rural economic panic and devise rescue strategies so that the countryside can have hope of revival. Then the foundation of the national economy can be consolidated, which is also our preparation for revenge."

Local Correspondence

Chongming

Three People Infected and Died in the Ship: A certain family in the western countryside of the county had an eight-year-old child who died of cholera at the home of relatives in Shanghai. The other day, three members of the family went to Shanghai to bring the child's coffin back to Chongming on the Dayun steamboat yesterday. After the ship left Shiliupu Guanqiao, before long, one of them suddenly contracted cholera. By the time it reached the Wusongkou, it was too late to save him, and he died. The other two also contracted the disease and died in the town and harbor of the county seat. It is indeed tragic that three members of one family died of the epidemic.

Confiscation of Smuggled Opium Pills: A certain inspector stationed at the Qiyao port of the Fifth Brigade of the Anti-Smuggling Unit of the Suzhou District in Chongming was selling red opium pills between Shanghai and Chongming, making considerable profits. The other day, a certain person carried a large quantity of opium and red pills at Pier No. 10 of Daguanqiao in southern Shanghai, intending to take a boat back to Chongming. This was detected by a certain inspector of the Shanghai Special Municipal Public Security Bureau's pier. The inspector boarded the ship for inspection and seized both the person and the goods, and brought them back to the bureau. The next day, he was sent to the local court for interrogation.

Songjiang

Absconding with Stolen Money, Arrested in Xinzhuang: Zhu Baosan, a fellow from Xiashi and partner at Gu Wanyun's second-hand clothing store in Huayang, eastern suburbs, had been employed for many years and had always been considered honest. Recently, the store's new boat brought back more than 800 yuan from Shanghai. The partner was blinded by greed, found the key in the accounts, secretly took the money, and quietly left the store, whereabouts unknown. After the incident, the store owner immediately notified various places to investigate by long-distance telephone. It was then learned that the runaway partner was arrested by the police in Xinzhuang Town. According to his confession, after leaving the store, he walked to Xinzhuang, intending to take a car to Shanghai. Now, Hua Wenren, the patrol officer of the Xinzhuang branch, has prepared a document to be sent to the Songjiang County Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Resolution of the Resignation Case of Firefighting Members: The carelessness of the Dafeng Silk Store on West Street extended to the neighboring Tang Sanju Shoe Store. Subsequently, the shoe store owner made proposals regarding the post-disaster firefighting policy to the County Chamber of Commerce. Upon hearing of the original proposal, the firefighting members believed that it was insulting and unanimously decided that the store owner must publish an apology in the newspaper. After several negotiations, there was no result, which caused all the firefighting members to resign, resulting in a major dispute. It is now learned that this case has been mediated by mediators, and the store has agreed to publish an apology in the newspaper. The dispute between the firefighting association and the shoe store owner has also been resolved.

Suzhou

Grain-Borrowing Uprising in Zhenze Township: Zhenze Township, under the jurisdiction of Wujiang County, has a population of 16,000 to 17,000 households. Due to the failure of silk cocoons this year, the rural economy collapsed, causing more than 10,000 households to have difficulty making a living. The other day, more than 400 villagers flocked to a certain rice shop in the township, claiming to borrow 500 dan of rice, and forcibly took food from nearby food stores. The security team police came out to maintain order, and fortunately, there was no uprising. Subsequently, Wang, the county magistrate of Wujiang County, personally went to the town and convened a meeting of gentry and representatives of the people, and decided to allow each township to borrow 2,500 dan of rice to the villagers, but the township chief must be responsible for repaying it in winter. The funds will be raised by the gentry.

Brothel Keepers Beat Up Military Police: Prostitution and gambling in Suzhou have been ostensibly suppressed, but this is not the case in reality. Gambling dens such as those in Niujiaobang are still gambling heavily, there are still more than 100 opium dens, and prostitutes are everywhere. The other night (the 16th) at about nine o'clock, a certain military police inspector went to a brothel at No. 11 Lerongfang to investigate whether there were any soldiers prostituting there. He was scolded severely by a brothel keeper. At that time, they were taken to the police station where a peaceful settlement was reached. On the afternoon of the 17th at six o'clock, six military policemen went to inquire about what had happened the previous night. Unexpectedly, the brothel keeper, Xing Gen, gathered more than ten people, including Da Jinzi, and dragged the six military policemen to Fangli Lane and beat them severely. Fortunately, a neighbor reported to the police district, and the police were dispatched and arrested Yao Xinggen, Da Jinzi, Chen Baosan, Yao Zhou, and two other suspects and sent them to the police district for review and handling.

Cabby Rapes Eleven-Year-Old Girl: Li Ziwei's daughter, Jin Nan, age eleven, who lives in Tonglefang outside the Loumen gate, was discovered by her mother the other day with bloodstains on her crotch and behaving strangely. She was asked about it, but she steadfastly refused to tell the truth. When pressed, she finally said that on the 13th, she was lured by a cabby named Guo Zhichang to an open space in Sanliuwang and raped. Upon hearing this, Li Ziwei immediately searched everywhere and found Guo on the road at ten o'clock last night and took him to the police station. Guo confessed that there were more than ten children playing on my car in Tonglefang, so I pulled them to Sanliuwang, but there was no rape, and other such statements. The police station immediately transferred the case of rape of a young girl to the general bureau for review and handling.

Wuxi

Extension of Time Limit for Redeeming Old Silk and Old Cocoons: The various money houses in our district had received a large number of old silk and old cocoons as collateral last year, and now the deadline has long passed. The mortgagors have delayed redeeming them, causing the financial stagnation of the various money houses, making it difficult to turn over. The money industry association has jointly requested the money industry association to convene a meeting of the industry to discuss and decide to limit the mortgagors to redeem from the various money houses before July 15. At the same time, it was submitted to the Department of Industry for record. After receiving the report, Director He immediately ordered the county to convene both the money and cocoon industries to properly discuss remedial measures. County Magistrate Chen convened the leaders of both industries at the Wenxi Hall in the county government yesterday morning (the 17th) to discuss everything. As a result, the silk and cocoon industry's request to extend the redemption deadline to the end of July was approved. The silk and cocoon industry association will notify its members to quickly find a way to redeem within the time limit, and at the same time appeal to the Department of Industry to find ways to provide relief.

Famine Relief Representatives Go to the Provincial Capital to Petition: The Temporary Famine Relief Association of our district held its fourth executive committee meeting at the County Chamber of Commerce yesterday morning (the 18th) at ten o'clock. The directors Cai Shisan, Chen Zhanru, Li Tiping, Gu Shuzhi, Hua Yinchun, Yang Chongyuan, Tu Keqiang, Qian Zhongliang, Hua Jianren, Gu Binsheng, Ni Xiangqing, and others were present, with Qian Sunqing presiding. (1) The representatives who were to be sent to the provincial capital to petition were originally scheduled to depart today to submit a petition when the provincial government convenes a meeting on Tuesday, striving to retain the allocation of construction land tax for special use. (2) Representative Gu Binsheng reported that regarding this petition, the petition procedures should be organized in detail, and the important points are currently being tabled regarding the rice grabbing cases in districts 7, 8, 9, and 14, so they will not be able to go to the province today. After the report, discussions began, and the following important cases were decided: (1)

Representatives Li Tiping, Chen Zhanru, Yuan Binsheng, and Gao Jiansi were scheduled to take a car to Zhenjiang at 6:00 p.m. on the 19th (Tuesday). (2) Each district should organize a famine relief branch to provide relief nearby. (3) Regarding the issue of receiving funds, each district head should submit to the county government for approval before jointly meeting with local fair persons to be responsible for receiving funds. (4) Prematurely use accumulated funds. (5) The famine relief areas should be based on the eight districts of 5, 7, 8, 9, 10, 15, 16, and 17, and the remaining four and six districts should be considered for handling.

Jiangyin

Public Security Branch Turmoil Subsides: A police officer in the first branch north of the city caused turmoil by accusing the branch chief, Li Mutang. On the 16th, County Magistrate Ma summoned more than ten leading patrolmen, including Li Chunshan and Hu Guirong, to lecture them in the main hall. Branch Chief Li Mutang has been transferred to the Qingyang second branch to exchange posts with Wang Hanchen. Patrol Officer Wang Hewu will exchange posts with General Bureau Patrol Officer Gu Shiming. Patrol Chiefs Wang Hongru and Jin Wenhai have been dismissed. The turmoil has come to an end.

Zhenjiang

Request to Punish Two Unlawful Officials: The Zhenjiang County Party Affairs Reorganization Committee stated that Chao Peizhi, a patrol officer of the Second Branch Office of the Third Branch Bureau of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, abused his authority and brutally tortured Zhang Defu, causing serious injuries. Nantong

Project to Salvage the Yuzhang Battleship Halted: The Ministry of the Navy hired more than 200 workers from Hubei to come to Nantong to salvage the Yuzhang warship in the Lujinggang river area. After more than 20 days, the ship had just emerged from the water when the rope broke and it sank back to the bottom of the river. Currently, the river water is rising sharply and it is impossible to proceed. The project has been temporarily suspended.

Inmates from Rugao and Haimen Prisons Transferred in Batches: The prisons in Rugao and Haimen counties have now been designated as sub-prisons of the Nantong Fourth Prison. Sun Xiong, the warden of the Fourth Prison, has gone to investigate the prisons. All male and female inmates who have been sentenced to more than three years will be transferred to Nantong, totaling more than 200 people.

Pinghu

News of the Closure of Dengying School: Dengying Elementary School in this city, originally named the First Elementary School, was established with donations from the Hu family during the imperial examinations. It has been in operation for more than 20 years. Since Principals Zhang and Xu took over, Zhang was dismissed due to a criminal case, and Xu ran away due to deficits. The school's affairs have deteriorated day by day. Last year, Feng Fukui took over, but there was no improvement. Now, after the provincial school inspector inspected the school, he submitted a report to the department requesting that the school be ordered to close. Its students will be merged into the nearby Danghu Elementary School, to reduce expenses.

Strange Phenomenon of Selling Japanese Goods: The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, in order to take care of the poor merchants, has allowed the merchants in this county who have Japanese goods to sell them all off within the month, and they will never be allowed to import them again. A certain amount will be extracted as anti-Japanese office expenses. However, since the start of the sale, more and more are being sold, and it is impossible to investigate. What is even stranger is that those whose original prices were more expensive but whose marked prices are low are all bought by relatives and friends and stored separately, so that they can be resold in the future under a different guise. The domestic goods that are slow to sell are put into the Japanese goods for sale. Also, most of them prepare two sets of books, cheating to avoid paying donations. Xu, the owner of a certain clothing store in Dongmen, is even more blatant, openly selling thousands of pieces of Japanese clothing materials imported from Shanghai. The industry has reported this to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association for handling.

Shaoxing

Homicide in Songxia: In Songxia, where Shaoxing and Shangyu meet, Wang Shuitang and Wang Yanliang, who are engaged in fishing, have long-standing grudges due to professional jealousy. The other day, in the afternoon, Wang Tingliang privately carried a handgun and shot Wang Shuitang to death. His son, named Erpang, was also seriously injured by the gun. The murderer immediately fled. The family has reported to the Shangyu Court, requesting that the murderer be arrested and punished.

Local News

Joint Committee Still Difficult to Conclude Immediately

Okazaki Visited Yu Hongjun Yesterday Morning to Discuss

The Issue of Troop Withdrawal from the Gongda and Toyota Factories

Since the Sino-Japanese ceasefire agreement, it has been more than two months since the deadline on the day before yesterday, and the Japanese army has finally completely withdrawn. However, there are still 20 to 30 Japanese soldiers stationed in the Gongda and Toyota yarn factories, so it cannot be said that the original state before January 28 has been restored. Yesterday, Okazaki, the Japanese representative of the Joint Committee, went to see Mr. Yu Hongjun to discuss this matter, and promised that after consulting with the military authorities, the remaining Japanese troops at the two locations would be withdrawn. The Joint Committee also indicated that this matter still needs to wait until a considerable period of time before it can be concluded. The news is published below:

Okazaki Visits Yu: Okazaki, the Japanese representative of the Joint Committee, visited Mr. Yu Hongjun at the Municipal Government at 11:20 yesterday morning. After the meeting, Okazaki asked Mr. Yu: (1) When the Japanese troops withdrew from District D the other day, what was the process like? Is the Chinese side satisfied with it? (2) After the Japanese troops withdraw, please pay attention to protecting the Japanese residents in the area. Mr. Yu replied at the time that the withdrawal was generally good, and that the Japanese residents living in the area would be protected by us because of our responsibility. The Japanese side need not worry about this point.

Troops Stationed in the Two Factories: Regarding the withdrawal of troops stationed in the Gongda and Toyota yarn factories, our side originally intended to propose it to the Joint Committee together with the withdrawal of troops from District D. However, because the Japanese side had already withdrawn troops stationed in District D, it was stopped. However, there has not yet been a formal reply to the Gongda and Toyota yarn factories, so Okazaki, after talking about the previous points, declared to Yu that the troops stationed in the Gongda and Toyota yarn factories were to protect the property of the Japanese there. The number of people is no more than 20 to 30 in each yarn factory, and they are only limited to being stationed indoors and cannot go out. Although the Japanese side believes that there have been a small number of Japanese soldiers stationed at these two locations before January 28, the Japanese side is willing to consult with the military authorities to withdraw as soon as possible, hoping that the Chinese side will be more understanding. After listening to this, Mr. Yu stated to Okazaki that if the Japanese side's statement is sincere, then the Chinese side will be understanding. Please give a sincere reply from the Japanese side in the near future, otherwise it should be submitted to the Joint Committee. At 11:50, Okazaki resigned.

Tasks of the Joint Committee: Regarding the handling of the conclusion of the Joint Committee, according to the New Voice News reporter's interview with the person in charge of the committee yesterday, it was learned that the committee believes that the work has not been completed because the Japanese troops at the Gongda and Toyota yarn factories have not yet withdrawn, based on the Sino-Japanese ceasefire agreement, and must wait until a considerable period of time before a meeting can be held to handle the conclusion. The reporter then asked whether the Japanese side had indicated a date for the withdrawal of the Gongda and Toyota yarn factories. The spokesperson said that the Japanese side believes that it has the right to be stationed in the above two yarn factories, but the Chinese side requires its withdrawal. Therefore, the conclusion date of the Joint Committee cannot be realized at present. According to another spokesperson, according to the ceasefire agreement, the Gongda and Toyota yarn factories must be withdrawn. Although the Japanese side intends to stay for a long time, this is difficult to achieve in fact. The conclusion of the Joint Committee must be the complete withdrawal of Japanese troops to restore the original state before January 28. Therefore, the Japanese troops at the Gongda and Toyota yarn factories have not withdrawn, so it cannot be considered that the original state of Japanese troops before January 28 has been restored.

The Takeover Committee Held a Closing Meeting Yesterday

Will Publish the Takeover Record to Announce Everything

The Japanese army stationed in Shanghai began to withdraw one after another after the signing of the ceasefire agreement. From May 5 to the day before yesterday, all Japanese soldiers have withdrawn. The Troop Withdrawal Area Takeover Committee organized by our side has also completed the takeover matters, so it is scheduled to end on the 24th of this month. Yesterday, the committee also reported the withdrawal situation in District D to the Executive Yuan. The details are recorded below:

Report to the Executive Yuan: After receiving District D tomorrow, the committee reported the entire process to the President of the Executive Yuan, Wang Jingwei, by telegram yesterday, because all tasks have been completed. The report included the withdrawal of the Japanese troops from District D, our takeover matters, and the general situation of the previous process, which was quite detailed.

Yesterday's Meeting: The Takeover Committee held a closing meeting at the Joint Society on West Ames Road at 5:00 p.m. yesterday. The attending members were Guo Dehua, Wen Yingxing, Zhu Xibo, and four others. Han Deshen did not attend due to business. The meeting discussed the closing matters, and as a result, it was decided to close on the 24th, and it was also decided to hold a simple closing ceremony at the time of closing. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 p.m.

Announcement of the Process: After the committee closes on the 24th, although the takeover of Zhabei, Yinhang, Jiangwan, Wusong, and other places has been disclosed in detail in various newspapers, there are still some points that have not been fully covered. Therefore, it is planned to publish a rare and systematic takeover record, announcing everything from the start of the Japanese army's withdrawal to the completion of the withdrawal, including all documents, inheritance, re-acceptance, and photos, etc., without exhaustive collection. It is expected to be published around the time of closing.

Disposal of Staff: The establishment of the committee was temporary in nature. When it was first established, it was jointly formed by staff members from various agencies, and many special commissioners and clerks were hired. Since the committee has ended, these staff members will be dismissed. However, the members will all return to their original positions in principle. For example, Director Yin Rugeng originally served as a counselor in the Municipal Government, Wen Yingxing originally served as the director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Guo Dehua originally served as the secretary of the Ministry of Finance, Zhu Xibo originally served as the section chief of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and Han Deshen originally served as the secretary of the Jiangsu Provincial Government.

Qian Zhongfu Talks About the Plight of Overseas Chinese in Nanyang

Sugar Transport from Java Sharply Reduced

Chinese Goods Plundered by Japan

After the outbreak of the Shanghai war, all industries have been affected, and shipping merchants are particularly affected. The Shanghai to Nanyang Islands route has been relatively prosperous in peacetime due to the transportation of sugar from Java and the travel of overseas Chinese. Now, its business has also declined. Mr. Qian Chongfu, a shipping merchant in Shanghai, made a special trip to Nanyang to inspect business affairs, inspect the sugar industry, and pay attention to overseas Chinese affairs. He has now returned to China and told reporters that the overseas Chinese in Java have suffered losses in the sugar industry and are unable to stand on their own. This matter is very important and must be retold as follows:

No One Buys Spot Sugar: Mr. Qian set off on June 9 and returned to China yesterday. This trip first went to Wangjiaxi, Surabaya, Sanbaolong, Jinglidan, Wanlong, Maowu, and Batavia. All major commercial ports in Java have been visited. The Java market is dominated by sugar production, 19% of which is in the hands of overseas Chinese. This year, the Shanghai war broke out, and the Yangtze River cannot transport sugar to the interior due to banditry. In addition, the silver and money industry does not release funds and has stopped handling sugar. After April, the import tax on sugar is 13 yuan and 5 jiao per dan, which is one and a half times higher than the price of sugar, resulting in the Java sugar market having no market price at all. The current stock of spot goods exceeds 2 million tons.

Sugarcane Fields Set on Fire: Since March, overseas Chinese firms in Java that operate the sugar industry have suffered unprecedented blows and have closed down one after another. Only two remain open. Most of the sugarcane fields in Java are owned by overseas Chinese. This year, when the sugarcane matured, many were unwilling to harvest it and make sugar because there was no way to sell the sugar. It would cost more than ten yuan per dan. When Mr. Qian was in Java, the overseas Chinese decided to set fire to the sugarcane planted in the fields. The flames soared into the sky and continued for several days.

Export Goods Seized by Japan: The largest exports from China to Java are cloth and soybeans. Now these two businesses have been taken away by the Japanese. After the three northeastern provinces were occupied, soybeans were transported from Dalian to Java, and piece goods were shipped from Japan. According to the leaders of the overseas Chinese in various parts of Java, overseas Chinese abroad are insulted in every way without the protection of a strong and powerful government. The motherland is in constant turmoil, and overseas Chinese have no place to stand. At present, 18 or 19% of the overseas Chinese businesses in Java have been taken away by the Japanese.

More and More Overseas Chinese Returning to China: There are more than one million overseas Chinese in Java, mostly from Guangdong and Fujian. Only about 1,000 people are from Shanghai and Shandong. Originally, the power in the Nanyang Islands was entirely in the hands of the Chinese. After the outbreak of the Shanghai war this year and the decline of the sugar industry, in the past four months, the overseas Chinese in Java have only returned to China and not entered the country. Even if there are occasional trips, it is the smallest number. If the country cannot be unified and there is another civil war, the overseas Chinese in Java will have no place to stand. Qian Qun also said that there is no wasteland in Java, no theft in the markets, and the roads are very wide and well-maintained. The doors can be left unlocked at night and there is no theft. This is because the territory does not allow the stay of unemployed foreigners.

The Issue of Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan

Xu Kan Returns to Beijing to Report

The Money Industry Held a General Meeting Last Night

The issue of abolishing taels and changing to yuan has been decided in principle since Xu Kan, the director of the Coinage Department of the Ministry of Finance, was sent to Shanghai to discuss it. The situations of all parties are recorded separately below:

Mr. Xu Returns to Beijing: Since arriving in Shanghai, Xu Kan has repeatedly discussed everything with various circles in Shanghai. He also held a meeting at the Central Bank last week to discuss the issue of abolishing taels and changing to yuan with Bei Songsun, Liu Hongsheng, Han Jingzhou, Hu Bijang, and others, deciding on the unification of the currency system and the manufacture of new coins, etc. Xu has been in contact for a long time and has obtained a result, so he will return to Beijing tomorrow night to report to the Ministry of Finance and then decide everything.

Contact Before Departure: Mr. Xu is going to Beijing with many important written opinions from all parties regarding the abolishment of taels and changing to yuan. He will also summarize the contributions of the bankers, and before leaving, for the sake of caution, he will contact Chen Xing of the Central Bank, Bei Songsun of the Bank of China, and others to discuss other unresolved issues. The results are all kept secret and cannot be announced.

Song Will Come to Shanghai: After Director Xu goes to Beijing, he will report the results of this contact in Shanghai to the Ministry of Finance. The reporter from Xin Sheng News learned from the banking industry yesterday that Song Ziwen, the Minister of Finance, must also come to Shanghai within days to discuss the central government's opinions with the banking industry, and then make a final decision.

General Meeting of the Money Industry: The local Money Industry Association has expressed six opinions after the financial authorities announced that this issue will be re-implemented, and submitted them to the government for adoption. At 7:00 p.m. last night, an extraordinary general meeting of members was also convened to discuss this case. More than 100 representatives from various banks, including Qin Runqing, Yu Zuoting, and Li Zishan, attended. In addition to discussing various cases such as members' debts, the issue of abolishing taels and changing to yuan was discussed for a long time. According to Yu Zuoting, a standing committee member of the association, who spoke to the National News Agency reporter at the meeting last night, the money industry is in favor of abolishing taels and changing to yuan if it is to achieve a unified currency system. If the government has no standard measures for this case in advance, and implements it rashly, the financial world will inevitably experience great terror in the near future.

Ministry of Justice to Revise the Shanghai Special District Court Agreement

To Make it a Purely Chinese Court

Free From Foreign Interference and Restraint

The New Voice News Agency said that the Local Court of the Special District of the Public Concession in Shanghai is the reorganized former Provisional Court. At the beginning of the establishment of the court, it was taken back from foreigners, so an agreement was signed with the relevant countries. Next April, the agreement will expire, and the Ministry of Judicial Administration is preparing to revise the agreement so that it will no longer be restricted by foreigners and become a purely Chinese court. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency went to the court to inquire yesterday, and the information obtained is recorded as follows:

Court Retrospective The Shanghai Special District Court was first established during the late Qing Dynasty, and was called the Mixed Court. It specialized in hearing Chinese cases and Chinese-foreign cases that occurred in the Public Concession. At that time, the judges were jointly judged by Chinese officials and consuls, but the power was in the hands of the Chinese officials. Since the rise of the Revolutionary Army and the establishment of the Republic of China, the presiding judge of the court, a Manchu, fled in the night, and there was no one in charge of the court. The Public Works Department took over and paid all the arrears of wages of the court staff, and at that time, the power fell into the hands of foreigners. Since then, all trials have only listened to the consuls, and from time to time, the spirit of our country's laws has been destroyed, and a malformed judicial institution has been formed. Although our authorities have strived to recover it, it has been to no avail.

Preliminary Recovery In 1926, during the era of Sun Chuanfang, representatives were sent to negotiate with consuls of various countries to implement the takeover. The result was that the takeover was implemented in the following year (1927), and it was reorganized into a provisional court for a period of three years. Its organization was like the era of the Mixed Court, only the power of judgment was in the hands of our Chinese judges. However, when the police station brought Chinese-foreign cases, the consular jury still appeared in court to participate in the judgment. In addition to the judge's instructions, the foreign consul's signature was still required, and the power of arrest and investigation remained in the hands of the police station. What we recovered was only a part of the right of judgment. At that time, the deadline was three years, and then a further reorganization was carried out.

Current Situation In 1930, the term of the Provisional Court expired. Xu Mo and others were sent by the Ministry of Judicial Administration to negotiate with the consuls of various countries to revise the agreement. On April 1st, the agreement was established and reorganized into the Special District Local Court. The appellate agency for second-instance cases of the Provisional Court was originally the Court of Appeal, but now it has been reorganized into the Second Branch of the High Court, and everything inside is more advanced than in the Provisional Court. All kinds of judicial powers are completely handled by our side. The unique points from the previous one are the cancellation of the consular jury system and the recovery of the coroner's office. What is still inferior to a purely Chinese court is that the rights of the police are in the hands of the police station. Police officers are all recommended by the police station. Although the court has a prosecutor's office, due to the relationship of the agreement, only Articles 103 to 186 of the criminal law are investigated and prosecuted by the prosecutor. The remaining articles are still handled by the police station.

Proceeding with Revision Recently, the Ministry of Judicial Administration has prepared to discuss the revision of the agreement with the relevant countries when the agreement expires on April 1 next year. According to Wei Wanqian, the clerk of the court, the Ministry of Judicial Administration has not yet issued an order on the revision of the agreement. Generally, when the revision is made in the future, the first step is to make the police power convenient for the court to command and not be restricted. The others are the exercise of prosecutorial power, etc., to make it a purely Chinese court.

Fundamental Issues The reporter then visited a senior official of the court, who said that after the expiration of the agreement, the revision of the agreement should be carried out. Police power is also an important issue, but the fundamental issue is still the recovery of the concession. Although the judicial police in the current court are employed by foreigners, the number is small, only more than 20 people. Even if they are recovered in the future, there will only be more than 20 people, and the search and arrest outside must be assisted by the police station. The court cannot directly command.

The Food Committee Resolved on Measures to Regulate Rice Prices

Requesting the Municipal Government to Purchase Large Quantities of Rice

Requesting the Central Government to Impose a Tax on Food Imports

The Municipal Food Committee held its 35th regular meeting at the Social Affairs Bureau at 2:00 PM on the 16th. The attendees were Zhang Laihui, Wu Guiyu, Sun Yongyi, Wu Juenong, Zhu Zixiang, and ten other members. Those attending as observers included rice industry representatives Gu Xinyi, Fu Zisheng, Fu Qiangeng, and three others. Chairman Zhang Laihui and recorder Zhou Minggang performed the formalities. First, the chairman reported (1) that the resolutions of the previous meeting had been submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau for approval, (2) that the postponement of the implementation of the new municipal peck system had been ordered to be difficult to approve, (3) that the rice of the storage association had lost more than 200,000 yuan according to the current market price, and it was proposed to sell it off with pain, which had been submitted to the municipal government for approval, (4) that committee member Ye Huiwen had many plans for the association's affairs, and had passed away due to illness yesterday, and all committee members were requested to stand in silence to express their condolences. Then, they discussed the proposal by committee members Zhu Zifan and Yan Xiaoquan that rice prices had plummeted, and farmers and merchants were frequently going bankrupt, so the municipal government should be requested to find a way to maintain it, and the proposal by committee member Gu Fu to request that rice merchants be persuaded to stop fresh rice, which were of the same nature, were discussed together. Measures to regulate rice prices were immediately resolved. (1) Submit to the municipal government to request the Shanghai and Baoshan counties should allocate a part of their accumulated funds to borrow cash from the silver and money industries to purchase rice in storage to maintain market prices. At the same time, rice merchants will voluntarily donate a storage fund of five cents per stone for a period of two years as a guarantee. If there is a loss, the money will be used to offset it. If there is a surplus, it will be allocated to the storage fund to complete the city's rice warehouse. (2) According to the old case of the association, submit to the central government to instruct the financial organs to levy a tax on food imports to show restrictions, and submit them for separate handling.

Xu Guangde Discusses Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan

Our country's currency system regulations were promulgated and implemented as early as the third year of the Republic of China. In theory, the national currency should be based on silver yuan as the standard currency. Today, there should be no more questions about abolishing taels and changing to yuan. However, in fact, in Shanghai, the sycee tael is used as the calculation currency standard, and its power is far above the silver yuan. Due to the shift in Shanghai's trade power, various ports along the Yangtze River and the coast almost recognized the sycee tael as an indispensable calculation standard. In the spring and summer of this year, suddenly due to various reasons, the market price of silver yuan has fallen from seven qian three fen to about six qian eight fen. The general financial circles are thinking of saving this situation, and they all agree that taking advantage of this opportunity, we should resolutely abolish taels and change to yuan, and consult with the central authorities to proceed with steps in order to realize it. From this point of view, its motivation is to save the market price of silver yuan and avoid further decline. Its purpose is to unify the currency system. The method is appropriate and there is nothing to discuss. What I want to discuss now is not whether to reform, but the advantages and disadvantages of the reform. The sycee tael is a virtual standard, and the reason why its circulation power can last for a long time must have its reasons for existence. My opinion is that the reason why the sycee tael can maintain its circulation power in our country's largest commercial port for a long time is nothing more than the following three reasons: (1) All circles in Shanghai are deeply rooted in the habit of using sycee taels. (2) The intermediaries in the general financial circles in Shanghai have special interests in silver. (3) Throughout history, the government has had weak strength in reorganizing the currency system and has no consistent policy. Now, please explain the above three points and contribute my humble opinions, which are also a research material in the voice of abolishing taels and changing to yuan.

(1) Shanghai's Habit of Using Sycee Taels The reason why the sycee tael can occupy a great influence in Shanghai's business is that the international exchange rate has used the sycee tael as Shanghai's standard currency for nearly 80 years. Seventy-six years ago, Shanghai did not have the name of sycee tael for its currency. At that time, Chinese and foreign trade mostly used foreign currencies, and the most popular ones were Spanish and Mexican (i.e. foreign) silver yuan. At first, Spanish silver yuan was the most popular. Later, Spanish silver yuan gradually decreased. The existing goods were scarce, and the market price of water rose day by day. Compared with Mexican silver yuan, the water even rose to about 40%. Therefore, in 1856, Shanghai's merchants changed Spanish silver yuan from hard currency to accounting currency, named sycee tael. The hard currency in circulation on the market was Mexican silver yuan. At that time, one Mexican silver yuan was worth 7 jiao 2 fen 4 li 3 hao Spanish silver yuan. According to this ratio, one Mexican silver yuan was valued at 7 qian 2 fen 4 li 3 hao of sycee tael. Therefore, Shanghai's two units of currency started in 1856. Nearly 80 years have passed. Although the sycee tael is a virtual standard currency, its credit can be permanently maintained. There are still two reasons: A, cash reserves, B, the credit of money houses. Regarding point A, because the sycee tael is a virtual standard currency, if there is a considerable amount of silver bullion prepared, it will not be the lack of uneven color and weight. It is a kind of centripetal force in habit. Once the habit changes, there will be no difficulty. Regarding point B, the usual silver bullion reserves include raw silver and large bars of silver, which account for less than one-tenth of the sycee taels received and redeemed in the market. The rest relies on the credit of money house notes to maintain turnover.

(2) Special Interests of Intermediaries in the Financial Sector The greatest interest of the money house in using both taels and yuan seems to be the handling fee of two hao and a half. This fee is calculated from each conversion, which is a huge amount. Once taels are abolished and changed to yuan, it will be completely sacrificed. In addition, money house notes have always been the most widely circulated credit currency in Shanghai's import trade. The power of banknotes issued by Chinese banks is far less popular than money house notes. On the one hand, it is said that the money house is an organization with unlimited liability, but a part of the reason is that the source of money house notes is very far away. The general social belief is that money house notes can represent sycee taels. Once sycee taels are abolished, the circulation of bank notes may also increase. The money industry may be affected in another way in terms of business. Foreign banks have always used sycee taels as the standard currency for international exchange. If taels are abolished and yuan are used, there is no major relationship, but there is less a virtual standard currency in exchange, which is less than the two conversion opportunities of sycee taels and silver yuan before the reform. In terms of collection and payment procedures, there is one less handling fee. This is the general situation of the special interests of sycee taels and intermediaries.

(3) The Government's Weak Strength in Reorganizing the Currency System and Lack of Consistent Policy When it comes to the government, the minting of silver coins is handled by the central government. All mints are under the jurisdiction of the central government. If the color and weight are handled seriously, it is not impossible to completely unify the silver yuan. The reason why foreign merchants opposed abolishing taels and changing to yuan in the past was that the central government was weak, and the mints in various provinces manufactured themselves without unification. Once the silver yuan becomes the unit of currency exchange in various countries, if there is a slight difference in the color and weight of the standard currency, it will inevitably affect international trade. This reason can no longer be established now, because in fact, our country's silver coins have all been handled according to the standard color of the sycee tael stipulated in the currency system regulations, but there are still things that should be considered. How much hard currency is currently circulating in the market in our country? Although the Ministry of Finance has not released accurate statistics, according to general estimates, it is about 170,000,000 yuan. If this number is correct, whether it is enough is still a question. If there is not enough hard currency, it must be supplemented with banknotes. We must unify the right to issue them and strictly determine the reserve method. Otherwise, we are afraid that there will be incidents of excessive issuance of banknotes, which will affect the soundness of the silver standard.

To sum up the above three points, Shanghai is the financial center of the country. Silver and foreign currency have been used for decades. The general public knows that it is a malformed currency, but since it has become a habit, once it is abolished, there will naturally be many inconveniences in the transition, and we should endure a little pain and agree to it. The money industry should also understand the trends of modern times, resolutely give up the special interests in the exchange of silver taels and silver yuan, and cooperate with the government and domestic banks to achieve the goal of unifying silver yuan. As for the government, it should also promptly urge the Shanghai Mint to realize the start of production of coins, in order to permanently maintain the standard color and weight of silver yuan. On the one hand, the mints in various provinces, such as the Tianjin, Nanjing, and Hangzhou plants, should be designated as branches of the central mint, or merged in order to unify them. At the same time, we must urgently crack down on the excessive issuance of banknotes to avoid the occurrence of unsound conditions in the currency system.

The Labor Dispute at the Anlu Cotton Weaving Factory Was Settled Through Mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau

A Peace Treaty Was Signed Yesterday, Totaling Four Items

After a labor dispute occurred at the Anlu Cotton Weaving Factory on Yuezhou Road, all the workers occupied the factory. The police went to intervene and there was a conflict. In order to avoid the expansion of the dispute, the Social Affairs Bureau convened mediation yesterday and signed a settlement. The details are recorded below.

Mediation Conference When the Mediation Committee held a mediation meeting at 10:00 AM yesterday, Xiang Limin, Yu Yifu, Yan Yusheng, and Mao Guomo from the Anlu Cotton Weaving Factory and the Fourth District Cotton Weaving Industry Trade Union were present. Wang Guangqing, chairman of the Social Affairs Bureau, and lawyer E Sen represented the employer. The chairman stated that he had been instructed by the municipal government that non-industry people should not act as representatives in labor disputes, so he changed to an observer. Then, the discussion began. It was not until 1:00 PM that the labor and management parties agreed to a settlement.

Original Record The original record of the mediation of the Shanghai Municipal Labor Dispute Mediation Committee. The disputing parties were the matter of closure and dismissal disputes. The committee convened mediation and the parties agreed to sign a peace treaty, which is recorded as follows: (1) The employer is allowed to dismiss all factory workers Yan Yusheng and others due to business losses and bankruptcy. (2) Each of the dismissed workers will be given a dismissal subsidy by the employer equal to 48 days of wages. (3) Piecework wages will be calculated based on the average of the last two months. Leave will be excluded, and yarn waiting will not be deducted. (4) If the factory resumes business in the future, it must give priority to hiring old workers. Chairman Wang Xianqing, members Yan Yusheng, Mao Guomo, Jin Yifu, Xiang Limin, recorder Wang Rangyu.
