They sent representatives Zhang Hongtong and others to pay a visit, and Section Chief Wang Shaojie received and answered each item: (1) The release of the arrested workers is a judicial matter and has been sent to the court. It is only allowed for the municipal government to send a letter to the court to leniently handle the workers who have been unjustly accused. (2) The labor dispute has been ordered by the Social Affairs Bureau to mediate properly, but the petitioning workers insisted on immediate release. Later, they were dispersed by police officers. Then, the workers gathered on the road behind the Finance Bureau.

Dispersed in the Afternoon The Dafeng petitioning workers gathered at the municipal government and insisted on not leaving. Zhu Xuefan, Li Yongxiang, and other members of the Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions went to the municipal government at 11:00 AM yesterday to visit Secretary-General Yu Hongjun and find a way to dredge the situation in order to resolve it as soon as possible. Secretary-General Yu replied, requesting that the issue of restoring the jobs of unemployed workers has been ordered by the Social Affairs Bureau to handle it, hoping to advise the workers to wait patiently for the processing. The issue of assaulting police officers is an insult to administrative staff, and the municipal government has sent it to the local court for handling according to law. However, the request for bail has been sent to the court, and the municipal government cannot comply with it, but the workers' knowledge is simple, and the municipal government is very forgiving. Therefore, it has notified the court to consider the situation and leniently handle it. Then, the Federation of Trade Unions tried its best to persuade the workers, and they dispersed at 1:00 PM in the afternoon.

Municipal Government Instructions The Municipal Government obtained information from the petitioning workers of the Dafeng Dyeing and Weaving Factory requesting to restore the work of 108 workers who were unemployed due to the war. In order to resolve it quickly and avoid the expansion of the labor unrest, it specially instructed the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday to properly mediate. It is heard that the bureau, after receiving the order, has decided to handle it according to law in the shortest period. Xu Yefu, chief of the Third Section, has designated staff to handle it.

Regarding Rent Reduction, a Re-examination of Rent Reduction Measures is Requested

The Municipal Citizens' Rent Reduction Movement Committee, considering the four rent exemption standards announced by the Municipal Government on the 8th of this month to be biased and unfair, has presented the facts and earnestly requests the Municipal Government to retract its decree and formulate a new one. Simultaneously, it has also submitted a request to the Municipal Party Headquarters, urging a unified stance to comfort the people's hopes. The original text is recorded as follows:

Submitting a report that the announced rent exemption standards are biased and unfair, presenting the facts, and earnestly requesting a retraction of the decree and a re-formulation to ensure fairness and comfort the people's hopes. On the 9th of this month, the report stated that your esteemed government's No. 28 announcement outlined four rent exemption standards. After reading them, the public was bewildered. In recent days, various groups of tenants from Zhabei, Pudong, the Nanshi, and the Central District have come to the association to question and express indignation. The association, after carefully considering the situation and based on past facts, also feels that the standards set by your esteemed government are biased and unfair, easily leading to disputes. Regarding what we have observed, we state the following: (1) In the areas of Wusong, Jiangwan, and Zhabei, your esteemed government stipulates a three-month rent exemption. However, the Japanese army invaded on January 28th, so the so-called three months should refer to February, March, and April. However, investigations reveal that our side did not complete the takeover of Wusong and Zhabei until June 17th. Before the takeover was completed and the Japanese army had not completely withdrawn, the tenants in the Wusong and Zhabei areas, according to the legal principle of "use and benefit," found it difficult to use and benefit from their residences in May and June. Now, they are unexpectedly required to bear rent from May onwards, which is truly perplexing. (2) In the special district north of the Suzhou River and west of Yokohama, your esteemed government stipulates two and a half months. The area north of the Suzhou River and west of Yokohama refers to the Hongkou area. This area was the Japanese army's operational base. The various cruel actions have been reported in newspapers and are countless. Therefore, many residents have not dared to move back even after evacuation. Even in terms of shops, although the Central District announced the resumption of business on April 1st, this area barely opened its doors in early May. Therefore, the exemption of rent for May is also a matter of course. (3) In the special district east of Yokohama, the Yangshupu area, only a two-month rent exemption is granted. The Yangshupu area was also a Japanese military operational base. The Public Grand Yarn Factory was the Japanese army's headquarters, and the situation was no better than in Zhabei and Hongkou. Therefore, normal conditions did not return in April. Why is only a two-month exemption granted? This is unfair. (4) The parts of South Shanghai and Pusong District north of the Suzhou River are generally exempted for one month, which is too vague. First, regarding South Shanghai, since the Japanese army invaded Zhabei, South Shanghai has been in frequent turmoil. Even your esteemed government and its subordinate bureaus and offices moved into the special district to work, which shows how critical the situation was. After the resumption of business on April 1st, the Nanshi area was still fearful day and night because the Japanese army in Zhabei had not withdrawn. It was not until the settlement was signed that the area became slightly stable. Therefore, the tenants' lack of use and benefit of their houses was probably not limited to one month in February. The part north of the Suzhou River is too broad and not fair. For example, the area around North Henan Road is also north of the Suzhou River. When did the Municipal Chamber of Commerce move back to work? This area was still in a state of terror in March. How could it be used and benefited? A one-month rent exemption is not fair. (5) The Central and Western districts of the Public Concession and the French Concession, as well as the Pudong area, are not included, which is unfathomable. If it is said that these two areas are safe areas, then the bombs that fell on Nanjing Road and Sichuan Road, the destruction of the Wing On No. 3 Factory on McTaggart Road, and the bombing of the French Concession were all common occurrences. Furthermore, shops were closed, factories were shut down, and the entire situation was no different from a war zone. It was clear that people could not live and work in peace. If it is said that it does not meet the regulations of use and benefit, then in the presence of enemy troops and flying shells, could the people's rental houses achieve the purpose of use and benefit, even though government organs were constantly moving? Or it is said, why didn't the tenants terminate their leases at that time? The transportation was obstructed at that time, and Shanghai was a place where people from all walks of life were mixed. Could leases be terminated with a single word? However, the fact that hundreds of thousands of people moved to other cities shows that it was not an absolutely safe area, but for the sake of the entire national spirit, long-term resistance, common defense against insults, and the decades of historical reasons for the Shanghai market, they could not all escape. Therefore, from the closure of the Central District from February to the resumption of business on April 1st, rent should be exempted at least according to this standard to be fair. Furthermore, regarding Pudong, although it was not a war zone, the bombing by airplanes was heard every day when the war broke out. Also, Japanese soldiers were stationed at companies such as Qichang Mitsui and Laobaidu Riqing. Japanese troops landed in places such as Takahashi. Therefore, the closure of shops and the evacuation of residents were undeniable facts. Why did your esteemed government regard them as outside the pale of civilization and not take them into account? The above statements are based on past facts and are in line with what your esteemed government calls "the use and benefit of the leased property is a prerequisite for the payment of rent, which is expressly stipulated in law and should be understood in reason." If it is not used and benefited, rent should naturally be exempted. This is the logical conclusion. Now, let us make another statement to your esteemed leader on the principle of rent reduction and exemption. A. Since the January 28th Incident, the social and economic situation has plummeted. The demand for rent reduction and exemption is nothing more than a remedy for the post-war economy, so as to ease the people's difficulties and facilitate their recovery. It is not intended to impose responsibility or burden on any party. Your esteemed government's announcement said, "The burden of this disaster should not be entirely placed on the property owners." In other words, the burden of this disaster should be entirely placed on the tenants? In short, during times of national crisis, all citizens should share both good and bad fortune, just as rights and obligations are equal to each other. Now, residents and shops have closed down, lost their jobs, and suffered losses due to the national crisis, which is already terrible. Property owners still enjoy income and bear no burden. In terms of the equality of rights and obligations, how can it be said to be fair? B. Your esteemed government's announcement said, "The property situation in this city is complicated, and the economic capacity of the property owners may not be as the residents say." This is even more perplexing. The property situation in this city is indeed complicated, but the reason for its complexity is that the property owners regard real estate as an investment business. Each transfer and each increase in value have created today's situation. This not only violates the essence of our Prime Minister's legacy of equalizing land rights, but also promotes the evil forces of capital monopoly. How should the revolutionary government fulfill its mission, strictly crack down on it, and prevent the Three Principles of the People from becoming a mere formality, so that the suffering of the people can be alleviated? Why should it only defend the interests of the property owners? Furthermore, since your esteemed government knows the economic capacity of the property owners, why doesn't it know the economic capacity of the tenants, and why doesn't it consider the overall social and economic capacity at present? Taking all these points into consideration, who would believe that your esteemed government is not partial to the property owners? C. Your esteemed government's announcement focuses on rent exemption and does not mention rent reduction at all. The high cost of rent in Shanghai is unprecedented in the country. The property owners use the excuse of increasing land value, but they do not know that the increase in land value is caused by the property owners using real estate as a speculative business. This kind of abnormal development should be suppressed, and especially after the war, the social and economic capacity is far from what it used to be. Rent should be reduced in a timely manner to alleviate the burden on the people. Nanjing, Hangzhou, Anqing, and other places also automatically reduced rent one after another in the rear. This city has suffered more than 30 days of artillery fire. Even if the rent reduction and exemption measures publicly formulated by the entire city are strictly implemented, I am afraid that the effect will not be much. Now, only a few months of rent is exempted. How can this make up for the recovery of industry and commerce? D. Renting a house is originally a contract, but rent reduction and exemption are not purely a rental dispute. According to the case of Tongchunfang, the court's judgment stated, "If the rent reduction and exemption movement can become a reality and be promulgated by a competent authority, it can be recognized as having the effect of excluding general laws. Then the tenant can deduct the rent." It clearly recognizes that rent reduction and exemption are not a legal contractual relationship. Otherwise, why would the promulgation of laws and regulations by the competent authority be able to exclude the effectiveness of general laws? Why would your esteemed government issue an announcement? Furthermore, in the previous talks convened by your esteemed government between property owners, tenants, and other relevant parties, Secretary-General Yu made the following statements: (1) The principle of receiving rent exemption is an indisputable fact between both parties. (2) The standards proposed by the Rent Reduction and Exemption Association will be given to the property owner representatives for reference, and a reply must be submitted before the 25th. (3) Before the announcement, all parties will be convened again to discuss and decide. Now, what has been announced violates the principle of rent exemption and has not fulfilled the promise of consultation and decision-making, resulting in criticism. The association also feels unable to explain itself. Therefore, we dare to state the various points and submit them to your esteemed leader, hoping that you will uphold your original intention of relieving the suffering of the people, retract the announced standards, consider the facts, solicit opinions from all parties, and formulate a new one to calm public anger and comfort the people's hopes. With the utmost urgency, we await your orders. Respectfully submitted to Wu, the Mayor of the Shanghai Municipal Government. (The document submitted to the Municipal Party Headquarters is the same, omitted.)

Local News II

Japanese Rogues Collude with Chinese to Sell Green Gas Guns

Seized at the New Hui Zhong Hostel

Three Japanese and Two Chinese Arrested

The Narcotics Division of the Shanghai Municipal Police, having recently learned that Japanese rogues were colluding with Chinese to organize a gun trafficking ring, possessing all kinds of military equipment and secretly selling green gas guns, which are strictly prohibited by the international community, dispatched detective Song Bingzheng, Chen Huiting, and Ding Yugao to act as military officers. They repeatedly went to Room 511 on the fifth floor of the Huizhong Hostel on Hankou Road to contact the leaders of the Chinese and Japanese smugglers to purchase a large number of military equipment. After more than ten days of negotiations, everything was basically ready, and they were only waiting to pay and deliver the goods. At 9:20 am yesterday, Song and other detectives, together with Pan Gentong, the Western Detective Chief, rushed to the hostel to investigate and arrest them. Three Japanese and two Chinese, Xu Zailin and Tian Chunyi, were arrested on the spot. Nine green gas guns, large, medium, and small, more than 200 bottles of green gas liquid, a submachine gun, more than 500 bullets, and several sample books of various pistols were seized and taken to the Old Gate Patrol Station. After questioning, the head of the patrol ordered the three Japanese to be handed over to the Japanese Consulate in Shanghai for interrogation, and the two Chinese, Xu and Tian, were temporarily detained. This morning, they were sent to the First Special District Local Court for interrogation. It is reported that the green gas gun does not require bullets and only uses liquid to fire. The large ones have a longer range and greater power. Once the other party smells the gas, they will immediately fall into a coma and sleep forever, unable to be rescued. The medium and small ones can also cause people to faint after smelling the gas, but they can wake up after six hours without any danger to their lives.

Noulens Case Summons Six Witnesses in Shanghai

Only Huang Wen Arrived

The Whereabouts of the Other Five are Unknown

The Noulens couple's case of endangering the Republic of China has been tried once by Li Mian, the criminal court president of the Jiangsu High Court, at the Jiangning Local Court. Currently, due to the various problems of the Noulens couple's hunger strike in Beijing, the request to transfer jurisdiction, and the request for bail for medical treatment, the second trial period has not yet been set by Judge Li. However, most of the witnesses in the case are in Shanghai. It is believed that six men and women, including Fei Jinshan, Zhao Yangshi, Ding Zhenxun, Zheng Bojin, Huang Wen, and Pan A'da, need to be summoned for questioning. Therefore, the Jiangsu High Court asked the Second Branch of the High Court in the First Special District to assist in summoning them by name. The Second Branch of the High Court issued summonses to the General Patrol Room based on the addresses of the witnesses listed in the documents, ordering them to be notified as soon as possible. However, more than a year has passed since the Noulens couple were arrested. Only Huang Wen still lives at the original address. The others have scattered and their whereabouts are unknown. Therefore, only Huang Wen complied with the summons yesterday morning and went to the Second Branch of the High Court, stating that he was from Guangdong, 53 years old, and the manager of the Xinghua Company. Judge Yu informed him of the reason for the summons from the Jiangsu High Court to testify in Beijing, saying that if he had to go by the deadline, otherwise he would be punished. Huang replied obediently and left. As for the five witnesses, including Fei Jinshan, who could not be found, the Patrol Room lawyer Li Zhishan went to court and stated that the Patrol Room would prepare a written report and submit it to the court so that the court could reply according to the situation. Judge Yu considered this method appropriate and adjourned the court.

Tragic Cry for Help in the Dark Night

A Female Corpse Discovered in the River

A Man Lying on the Bank

Wife's Infidelity Leads to Husband's Murder

Janitors and others at Jiangwan Central School were enjoying the cool air in the school the night before last, when they suddenly heard a sharp and tragic cry for help at around 10:00 pm, suspecting it was a robbery. They immediately sounded the alarm. The Fifth Precinct of the Fifth District heard the chaotic alarm and suspected that there was an extraordinary incident. They ordered the patrol leaders to search the surrounding area. They discovered a female corpse in the small river east of the school and a man lying on the ground on the bank. They immediately arrested him and took him to the station for interrogation. The man confessed that his name was Zhang Shouan and he lived in Hujia Muqiao. The deceased was his wife, Zhang Sunshi, 23 years old. Because of her infidelity, he brought her to this place, murdered her, and pushed her into the river. He heard the alarm and lay in the dark to escape, but he was seen by the flashlight. The police station detained Zhang and ordered the Baoshao to report the case to the local court yesterday. Prosecutor Yang An and Inspector Shen and others were commissioned to the scene and found that the deceased was wearing a white cotton short shirt and black gauze pants. There was dirty cloth on her lower body. Her neck and throat were broken, and there were several nail marks. It was determined that the murderer strangled her to death by breaking her throat. It is thought that the cry for help at that time was from the deceased begging for help and was the time when the murder was committed. The Baoshao was ordered to collect the body on behalf of the government, and the police station was ordered to send the case to the court for investigation.

Male and Female Corpses Embracing Each Other Discovered in the Huangpu River

Both Men and Women are from the Upper Class

There is a Name on the Flower Handkerchief

Apparently Sacrificed Due to Unrequited Love

The Water Patrol Room recovered a male and female youth corpses from Floating Buoy No. 16 the day before yesterday. The two corpses were tightly held together, and there was a trouser belt between them. The two corpses were tied together by this trouser belt, apparently a love suicide due to unrequited love. The detective Huang Songsheng was ordered to take them to the Putan of the Rescue Bureau at the South Wharf and report to the local court. Prosecutor Yang Qi and others identified the bodies as drowning and ordered them to be collected. The male corpse was in his twenties, wearing a white silk short shirt and pants. The female corpse was about twenty years old, wearing a white silk gown, both dressed in upper-class fashion. There was a flower handkerchief in the corpse bag with the words "Dear Brother Chengxun, Best Wishes, Sister Juying." It is presumed that the man was Chengxun and the woman was Juying, and the tragic death of love has become clear.

Creditors of Riyue Bank Oppose Immediate Auction of Huang Chu Jiu's Assets

Regarding the bankruptcy of the Shanghai Riyue Bank and the Great World Amusement Savings Department, the Second Special District Court has scheduled a general auction of all movable and immovable property of Huang Chu Jiu to repay debts and expedite the closure of the case, as previously reported. Lawyers Wang Shizong, Dong Yu, Dong Chi, Chen Zhigao, Bian Jialu, Qin Zemin, Xu Yannian, and Chen Tingrui, representing several thousand creditors, unanimously opposed the immediate auction. They jointly submitted petitions to the execution division of the Second Special District Court yesterday morning, stating to Judge Cao that they were pleased to learn from the newspapers of the 7th of this month that the court had ruled to implement the auction of Huang's assets. However, they noted that the court had held several hearings before the deadline, and the petitioners had not been summoned. Only Yan Luqing, a lawyer representing a portion of the creditors, had appeared in court to present arguments and make requests, which could hardly represent the intentions of all creditors. Furthermore, most of Huang's real estate is subject to mortgages. It is uncertain whether the auction proceeds, after deducting the mortgage debts, will yield a surplus or be insufficient to cover the mortgaged debts. Moreover, it is questionable whether the current disposition of properties built on leased land will secure favorable returns. All these matters are closely related to the interests of the creditors. Since the creditors and their representatives were not given the opportunity to consider the disposal methods before the fact, nor was their consent obtained afterward, in order to protect the creditors' interests from losses, they requested that the court summon all creditor representatives to present their opinions before disposing of Huang's assets, so as to safeguard the interests of the creditors. Judge Cao announced that he would summon them within the shortest possible time and ordered accountants Pan and Wu to submit detailed written reports for review, before adjourning the hearing.

Submissions to the Municipal Government from Various Branches of the Citizens' Federation

Similar Commercial Losses in the Central District

Request for Fair Treatment in Rent Exemption Standards

The 26th, 11th, 8th, 18th, and 24th district branches of the Shanghai Citizens' Federation, noting that the municipal government's recent promulgation of rent exemption announcements has overlooked the area south of the Suzhou Creek (Central District), failing to consider the suffering of businesses due to the strike, deemed it unfair. Yesterday, they jointly submitted a petition to the municipal government stating: "We petition to request consideration of the overall situation of the city, insight into the difficulties of businesses, and the promulgation of rent exemption measures for the area south of the Suzhou Creek (Central District) as well, to show that relief is universally applied and that fairness and facts are emphasized. When the January 28th incident occurred, the city unanimously went on strike to resist aggression for more than two months. The commercial losses are incalculable. Since the painful resumption of business on April 1st, the postwar commercial decline threatens bankruptcy. Therefore, an atmosphere of rent exemption pervades the entire city, hoping for its implementation to provide adjustment. Demands for promulgation are eagerly awaited. Unexpectedly, the announcement of rent exemption has greatly disappointed the people. The so-called weighing of the situation, deliberation of principles, and broad collection of public opinion are mere formalities. The Central District, which was equally affected by the war and suffered similar losses due to the strike, has been excluded from rent exemption, discriminating against public opinion and disregarding the people's livelihood. The public is bewildered by this. If prompt measures are not taken, it will be impossible to uphold public opinion and emphasize principles. The association, recognizing the difficulties of the commercial market and to prevent the proliferation of disputes, requests a two-month rent exemption to demonstrate fairness. We respectfully submit this document requesting review and approval for implementation, for the public good."

Record of Meeting of the United Association of Fellow Provincials Associations

The United Association of Fellow Provincials Associations in Shanghai held its third executive committee meeting at its association hall in Xinping Lane, Longmen Road, yesterday afternoon. Wu Guochang, Zheng Zhengqiu, Shi Yuemen, Weng Guoxun, Cheng Kexin, Song Shixiang (representing Wu Guochang), Cao Zhenqing, and Qian Liqun attended. Wu Guochang chaired the meeting, and Jiang Changjie served as the secretary. The following resolutions were passed: (1) In addition to the Economics Section being responsible for collecting membership fees, all committee members present today will first represent their respective associations and freely determine the amount. Those who did not attend will be sent letters requesting payment. (2) Publish the association's constitution and operating rules. (3) Prepare a budget for income and expenses. (4) Compile a list of committee members. (5) Petition the municipal government to revise the announced measures for rent reduction and exemption in a fair and impartial manner. (6) Set the date for a temporary general meeting at 5:00 PM on July 24th. The meeting was then adjourned.

News of Rent Reduction Dispute in Fuxing Lane, French Concession

Various organizations and tenants in the French Concession are paying close attention to the rent dispute in Fuxing Lane. In addition to sending a letter to the court requesting a fair trial, all tenants in the lane continued to hold an emergency general meeting at a tea garden in the city's Chenghuang Temple at 2:00 PM yesterday, with more than thirty people attending. First, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, followed by proposals from various tenant representatives: (1) The Third Tribunal of the Second Special District Court will continue the trial next Wednesday at 9:00 AM. Although only the Fuli Tai Beef Shop is suing, the case affects everyone, so everyone should attend the trial. Also, send letters to various organizations requesting them to send representatives to attend and observe. (2) All tenants have evidence that the landlord collected rental deposits. Each tenant has verified the ticket stubs with the Qianzhuang banks and will not recognize the landlord's changed rent terms. It is illegal to extort rent. Legal advisors Li Ming and Chen Chou will be asked to file a criminal lawsuit with the court. (3) Regarding the landlord's lawsuit for rent arrears, each tenant has a large deposit, which, according to the amount claimed, is more than sufficient. Furthermore, since May, each tenant has deposited the rent into the bank, so there is no reason for the claim in fact. The court should dismiss it and file a counterclaim. (4) Issue a declaration exposing the landlord's unreasonable oppression and profiteering by subletting and extorting rent, hoping to gain sympathy from all sectors of society. (5) In the name of the Tenant Federation, send letters to the Municipal Rent Reduction Movement Committee, the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Concession, the Citizens' Federation, and the various Road Business Federations to uphold justice and provide assistance. Declare that if the rent reduction requirement is not met due to complete evidence and reasonable demands, it will inevitably affect the city's rent reduction movement. (6) If necessary, the tenant association will petition the Municipal Party Department, the Municipal Government, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and the Municipal Council for Adjudicating Rent Disputes. (7) In the name of the Tenant Federation, schedule a dinner to invite representatives from various organizations, agencies, and Chinese consulates to report the true facts of the lane to facilitate external understanding. (8) Appoint three representatives in advance to report everything to the Rent Reduction Committee of the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the French Concession and the volunteer legal team. (9) Each tenant has thoroughly investigated the landlord's subletting and building costs and the fact that they are making large profits and has made a form, which will be sent to lawyers Li and Chen today for submission to the court for reference. (10) The reason why each tenant is participating in the rent reduction request is that they are affected by the expensive deposits, their businesses are not improving, they have suffered losses due to the war, and every family is finding it difficult to support themselves. If the goal cannot be achieved, then when necessary, they will all give up their leases to the landlord. There are already several businesses in the lane who have expressed their determination to give up their leases before the problem is resolved, such as the Yuedong Inn in the lane, whose business is poor, with a maximum of five or six yuan of business per day, which is not enough to cover daily expenses, let alone maintain the business in the past. Therefore, all middle- and upper-class inns in the French Concession are being liquidated and closed. This suffering is due to the influence of high rents. The other shops in the lane are also suffering the same pain, but the landlord does not show compassion and is oppressing each tenant, so they must fight to the end. All of the above proposals were approved by the crowd and the meeting adjourned.

Statistics on Visitors to Public Parks Managed by the Public Works Department

In June, the various parks managed by the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council had a total of 188,088 visitors, with the most visitors to Fanwangdu Park, accounting for more than 71,000. The next most popular was Pootung Park with more than 46,800. Hongkou Park had only over 18,000 visitors. The remaining Huishan, Jingwu, Singapore Road, and Kunshan Road parks, and children's parks had a total of more than 52,000 visitors.

Two Recent Rescue Efforts by the Municipal Ferry

One Russian woman... one Frenchman

Last Saturday (the 16th) at 1:00 PM, the Municipal Ferry No. 1 departed from the Bund of Nanjing Road. When it reached the vicinity of the Jianghai Customs gunpowder depot, a Russian woman suddenly jumped into the river from the stern of the ship, attempting suicide. Deputy Director Cao of the Municipal Ferry Administration happened to be on board and, upon seeing this, immediately threw four lifebuoys. He also ordered the ferry to reverse and circle back. Eventually, the sailors helped to rescue the Russian woman, gave her clothes to change into. He asked her the reason for the suicide, but she remained silent, with a look of sorrow on her face, revealing a kind of grief. Later, the woman waited for the ferry to dock and borrowed one yuan from the ship's staff before leaving.

The day before yesterday (Sunday) at 3:00 PM, a Frenchman, accompanied by friends and family, took the municipal ferry to the Gaoqiao seaside bathing beach. He did not swim, but sat on the beach, drinking a lot of alcohol. Suddenly, he fainted, and his limbs became rigid. A ferry staff member spotted this and immediately took out his own wire bed, helped him lie down, and the staff members, along with his family, tried their best to rescue him and took him to the hospital and found a doctor to treat him. However, he had already stopped breathing. The Municipal Ferry Administration then specially opened a boat to send him back to Shanghai. According to his family, the Frenchman had been ill for many days with a high fever. He was forced to come here by his friend's insistence. They expressed deep gratitude to the Municipal Ferry staff for their assistance.

Collision between Inland Ships in the Huangpu River

Fortunately, No Major Damage

The Yih Ho & Co's Shanghai-Yixing ship Jiang He, which arrived in Shanghai from Hankou on the 16th, was docked at the No. 22 river buoy near Tilanqiao. At 4:00 PM on the 17th, it changed to the No. 2 river buoy, untied the cable, and drove south. Near the river buoy, it was driving slowly to tie the cable. Unexpectedly, it was pushed by the rapid current, and the hull leaned toward Pudong. The Italian warship Esperia, which was moored there, saw the Jiang He colliding and was unable to move, so the Jiang He grazed it on the starboard side. Fortunately, the Jiang He was a small ship, and neither ship sustained major damage. The water patrol police dispatched a boat to the scene to investigate. The Jiang He itself was damaged by the collision, but the crew was unharmed.

Reactionary Elements Rotated for Preliminary Hearing

At the Gonghe Grand Theater on the corner of Caobao Road, Roberts Road, and Jiaozhou Road in West Shanghai, a group of reactionary elements gathered on the morning of the previous day under the pretext of raising funds to aid the Northeast Volunteer Army by staging a play. They convened a secret meeting of representatives of the Anti-Imperialist League of Jiangsu Province, distributed reactionary leaflets. Zhu Mingqin, the sixth district chief of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, dispatched patrol officers and police officers from the second battalion of the police force, along with Chinese and Western detectives from the Concession Police, and detained more than ninety people in the field, along with reactionary publications. They were transported in three trucks and presented to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for temporary detention. Details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. It has been learned that Wu Zhiquan, chief of the third section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, dispatched Ding Shibai, director of the interrogation section, along with four section staff members, to conduct preliminary interrogations in rotation. It is said that the case is serious and cannot be disclosed. After the preliminary hearing procedures are completed, the prisoners and their statements will be sent to the Garrison Headquarters for investigation.

Zhu Jiqing's Secretary Su Youxi Seriously Injured and Dies in Car Accident

Automobile Driver Zheng Yuqiu Also in Life-Threatening Condition

Zhu Jiqing, a member of the Central Committee, was travelling from Shanghai to Beijing and then to the Northeast. Because there were still unfinished matters in Shanghai, he left his private secretary, Su Youxi, in Shanghai to take care of everything. Yesterday morning at 9:35, Su was riding in a black Zhao Hui No. 726 car on official business. When the car drove to the front of the Wanguo Cemetery on Jing'an Temple Road, a trolley car from the first route of the British Concession was coming from the east. The trolley car came with great momentum and the two vehicles collided. The car was completely destroyed, the driver Zheng Yuqiu was injured in the heart and was spitting blood from his mouth. Su was most seriously injured in the head, his scalp was ruptured and he was bleeding profusely and was unconscious. The Jing'an Temple Road Fire Engine rushed him to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road and he was admitted to special ward No. 23. Doctor Ji Changgeng treated him. His temperature reached 39.6 degrees and he had lost consciousness. He died at 6:30 in the afternoon due to serious injuries and ineffective treatment. The car driver's injuries were also severe, and his life is in danger.

Conviction for Raping a Young Girl

Xu Caifu, age 39, was convicted for going to the home of his fellow villager Ge Ayuan at 44 Yuanfang Road from the 12th of last month to the 12th of this month. Under the pretext of playing mahjong, he enticed and raped Ge's 14-year-old daughter Youlin a total of eight times. Ge Dai, the girl's mother, found out about it and reported it to the Huishan police station. Detectives were sent to arrest Xu and bring him to the First Special District Local Court. After repeated inquiries, the judgment date arrived yesterday morning. Judge Shen Bingrong took the bench and announced the judgment. The defendant, Xu Caifu, was sentenced to three years and six months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized would be converted at a rate of two days to one day of imprisonment.

Suspicious Behavior of Concubine Leads to Assault During a Quarrel Over Cooling Off

Violently Attacked with Six Knives, Severely Injured

Wang Qian, a woman from Shaoxing, is 27 years old. She had a relationship with Wang Yanshan, also from Shaoxing, for seven years and lived together at 1990 Peng Road. In May of last year, she suddenly ran away. Wang found her on Tangshan Road. After that, Wang became suspicious of his concubine's runaway behavior and tightened his control, forbidding her from going out. At around 10:00 PM on the night before last, she wanted to go out to cool off because the weather was hot, but Wang did not allow it. At 10:45, she sneaked out. Shortly after, she came back after cooling off. Wang scolded her, and she argued back, which led to a quarrel. Wang took a kitchen knife and suddenly went forward and attacked her violently with six knives, causing her to sustain five injuries to her left leg and one injury to her left hand. Blood gushed out, and she fell to the ground, shouting for help. The second landlord, Lu Yonglin, reported it to the Huishi Police Station, which dispatched Chinese detective Tang Guangfu and notified the fire brigade to send a fire truck. Wang was arrested with the knife and taken to the police station, and the injured Wang Qian was taken to Guangren Hospital for treatment. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Second Criminal Tribunal of the First Special District Court. Police station lawyer Qian Xunjiu stated the previous situation, saying that the victim Wang Qian was seriously injured and was receiving treatment in the hospital, so she could not come to court. He requested a postponement of the interrogation and presented the murder weapon. Then, the witness Lu Wang, a woman, testified that at around 10:00 PM last night, she suddenly heard screams for help upstairs. She hurried upstairs and saw the defendant still holding a kitchen knife, while Wang Qian was lying on the ground. After Ge Sixun checked the confession, he questioned the defendant Wang Yanshan and ordered him to be detained for another seven days for further investigation.

Wang Yousheng Suddenly Arrested

Zhejiang Provincial Government Accuses Him of Falsely Accusing Farmers of Colluding with Bandits

Result: Released on Bail of 10,000 Yuan

Wang Yousheng (aka Wang Liuquan), a 55-year-old native of Shangyu County, Zhejiang, is a businessman in Shanghai with modest assets. He lives at No. 12, Lane 366, Bubbling Well Road, French Concession. The other day, lawyer Gu Changyuan, holding an arrest warrant from the First Special Court, went to the Xinzha Police Station to request the police to arrest Wang Yousheng. The reason for the arrest was that Wang had falsely accused farmers Chen Shijing and others of colluding with bandits in Zhejiang Province in February of last year. The chief then sent Chinese detective Su Yinggen to the French Police Station to cooperate with French detectives in arresting Wang. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Second Criminal Tribunal of the First Special Court. Chen Shijing hired Gu Changyuan and Tao Wuzhi as lawyers to appear in court. Wang Yousheng hired Fan Gang, Yu Chengxiu, and Tan Xinwan as lawyers to defend him. First, police station lawyer Qian Xunjiu stated that the defendant was suspected of making false accusations, so the Zhejiang Provincial Government requested the court to arrest him and requested permission to transfer him. However, the Zhejiang Provincial Government is not a modern court, so according to the agreement, the plaintiff should submit sufficient evidence. Until the evidence is proven, the police station is unwilling to transfer the defendant. Moreover, the Zhejiang Provincial Government did not send anyone to court today to make the request, so he requested a postponement of the interrogation. Then, lawyer Gu stated that the defendant was not only suspected of making false accusations in Zhejiang Province, but also of illegally establishing public cases and forcibly occupying sand fields. As the lawyer was about to speak at length, the defendant's lawyer immediately stood up and objected, saying that lawyer Gu had not submitted a power of attorney today and had no right to speak. He should be prohibited from speaking. Moreover, the Zhejiang Provincial Government is the highest-level administrative organ in Zhejiang Province and is not a judicial authority, so the Zhejiang Provincial Government has absolutely no right to hear this case. The points mentioned by lawyer Gu just now were similar to those of local tyrants. The regulations for punishing local tyrants have been explicitly abolished. According to the agreement, sufficient evidence must be submitted for proof. Since he has not submitted any, he should be released, or allowed to post bail to be available at any time. Because the defendant has lived in the concession for many years and is a legitimate merchant, there is no risk of him fleeing. After Judge Ge Sixun checked the report, he stated that this case was requested by the Zhejiang Provincial Government for assistance. Since the Zhejiang Provincial Government did not send any official documents, the case could not be clearly understood. He then ordered the defendant to post bail of 10,000 yuan in cash or by guarantor, pending the arrival of official documents from the Zhejiang Provincial Government for further investigation.

Chongming Bandit Arrested in Shanghai

Cao Aqing, a notorious bandit involved in the robbery of Zhang Sanjiang and other families in the Fifth District of Chongming County, has been wanted by the water and land police departments for a long time, but has not been apprehended. Recently, Mao Xiaoshan, a detective from the 17th team of the Fourth District of the Waterborne Public Security Team of Jiangsu Province, learned that the bandit was hiding on a coal boat outside the Taitong Wharf in Lujiazui, Pudong. He secretly reported it to Team Leader Gong, who prepared official documents and came to Shanghai yesterday morning to request the Third District of the Public Security Bureau to send police to assist in the arrest. The bandit was leaving the Longquan Tea House and was identified correctly by the informant. He was arrested on the spot and taken to the district. After Director Yu briefly interrogated him, the bandit confessed that he was 35 years old, a native of Chongming, and had no fixed address. He was ordered to be sent to the General Bureau for interrogation first and then the detective was instructed to take him back to the bureau for trial.

Father-in-Law and Son-in-Law in Violent Incident Over Unpaid Rent

He Jinyu, a carpenter from Yangzhou living at No. 30 Qijiabang, Jingzhou Road, lived with his father-in-law, Gu Yongchang, from Jiangbei. At 9:00 PM the night before last, Gu demanded four months of rent, totaling 14 yuan, but He refused to pay, causing a dispute. He went to his friend Zhou's place at No. 43 Baocheng Lane and obtained a chisel, with which he stabbed Gu in the left arm and punched him to the ground. Gu's son, Zhenrong, saw this and was shocked. When he went forward to dissuade them, he was also stabbed in the arm, chest, back, and other parts, injured and fell to the ground, bleeding profusely. He saw that he had caused a big disaster and took the opportunity to escape. After the police were informed, they immediately ordered Chinese detective Ma Wenda to investigate and sent the two injured to the Sacred Heart Hospital. Gu Yongchang's injuries were relatively minor. After the doctor bandaged him, he was discharged. When the murderer He Jinyu was arrested by the detective at No. 43 Baocheng Lane, he tried to escape and jumped out of the window on the second floor, injuring his leg. He was taken to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special District Court for interrogation. The police station lawyer stated that the victim Gu Zhenrong was seriously injured and could not attend the court. He requested a postponement. Gu Yongchang complained that the defendant was his son-in-law and lived in his house, owing four months' rent without paying a penny. When he asked for it, he dared to commit violence. His son Zhenrong tried to dissuade them and was also stabbed. He requested an investigation. His daughter He Gu stated that she had been married to the defendant for three years and had not yet had children. At that time, it was over the unpaid rent, and the defendant insulted and scolded her father, causing him to be slightly hit in the face. He went out to get a chisel and came home and stabbed her father. She did not witness it, however. When questioned, the defendant confessed that he had owed rent for four months, but there was a war in Shanghai, so he should be given three months' rent exemption. His wife had paid four yuan. At that time, his parents-in-law, his wife, and his brother beat him together. Unable to resist, he used a chisel to resist, etc. After Judge Shen Bingrong checked the confession, he ordered him to be returned to custody, pending the recovery of the victim for further investigation.

Laborer Drowns While Taking a Cold Bath

Lu Fulin, a 26-year-old native of Haimen, worked as a laborer for the Shanghai Moving Company. The day before yesterday afternoon, he went to the Suzhou Creek, south of Henan Road, to take a cold bath alone. He accidentally slipped and fell into the river, causing him to drown. His body sank to the bottom of the river. After Lu's wife, Wang, found out, she sent people to dredge for him. At 7:00 PM, the body was recovered near the silk merchants' wharf. That night, a coffin was prepared to take in the remains.

Yong An Tang's Hu Guigeng's Banquet for the Press Yesterday

With Sincere Remarks During the Gathering

Mr. Hu Guigeng of Tiger Balm Yong An Tang hosted a banquet for reporters from various newspapers at Xing Hua Lou on Fourth Malu last night. A large number of reporters attended and were warmly welcomed by Mr. Hu. After several rounds of drinks, Mr. Hu stood up and delivered a speech, saying, "I, on behalf of Mr. Hu Wenhu, the owner of Yong An Tang, have prepared this simple feast tonight to celebrate with the leaders of the press. I am honored and grateful for your presence. This banquet has three meanings, which I would like to share with you all. (1) The significant relationship between the press and society and the nation is well understood by the world and needs no further explanation from me. I have a great interest in this field. I have lived in Southeast Asia for more than ten years, and most of my time has been spent in newspaper offices. However, I am of mediocre talent and have achieved nothing. Only this interest has not diminished. Shanghai is the center of the nation's economy and culture, and Shanghai's newspapers are the center of national public opinion. You are all erudite and experienced, and you are the driving force behind this center of public opinion. Although I have only been in Shanghai for a month, I have always wanted to learn from you. Tonight, in the spirit of friendship over drinks, I take this opportunity to meet with the leaders of the press, who shape the national public opinion, to witness your elegance and hear your insightful views. It is truly a pleasure. (2) Mr. Hu Wenhu, the owner of our company, although raised in Southeast Asia, loves his motherland no less than others. He has always been the first to donate to various disasters in the country, such as floods and droughts. The Central Women and Children's Hospital in Nanjing was also built with his sole investment of over 370,000 yuan. He pays special attention to and respects the press and journalists. He has established the Burmese Morning Post in Yangon, the Star Daily in Singapore, and the Star Hua Daily in Shantou. Last year, he returned to China and planned to establish newspapers in Shanghai, Xiamen, Shantou, Hong Kong, and other places to serve as tools for communication between China and Southeast Asia and to encourage overseas Chinese to invest in China. Due to the turbulent times and the temporary lack of talent for running newspapers, he had to start with a trial in Shantou. His ambition has not diminished. During my return to China this time, Mr. Hu repeatedly instructed me to pay close attention to and engage with the press and its leaders in Shanghai in my spare time to learn from them for improving the newspapers in Singapore and other places. Mr. Hu is also eager for overseas Chinese to invest in the motherland, so he also hopes that I can report to you on the recent situation of overseas Chinese to encourage them, guide them, and support them in returning to China to start businesses. (3) Now, from the perspective of overseas Chinese, I would like to report to you on the situation of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia. Since the global economic crisis became serious, Southeast Asian businesses have also suffered a major blow. The unemployed are feeling the pain of displacement and lack of food and clothing, while the wealthy are also facing crossroads and difficulties in advancing and retreating. Staying means lamenting the lack of investment opportunities, while returning to China means feeling isolated. Their distress and crisis are truly unknown to outsiders. You are the guides of society, and I sincerely hope that in addition to writing about national affairs and criticizing political gains and losses, you will also pay attention to these pitiful overseas Chinese, encourage them to invest in China, guide them on investment paths, and awaken the sympathy and support of the people of the country. I urge the government to provide them with effective protection, which is within your authority and responsibility." After Mr. Hu's speech, the guests exchanged toasts and enjoyed the banquet until around 9 o'clock, when the guests and host parted happily.

Temporary Hospital Established at Jing'an Temple

Jing'an Temple Abbot Zhifa, considering the prevalence of epidemics after the war, believes that prevention and treatment should be prioritized. Therefore, he continues to run the Jing'an Temple Temporary Clinic Hospital as usual, appointing Long Yifei as the director. He is actively preparing to expand the scope, inviting renowned doctors Zhu Zhensheng, Chen Minsheng, Jiang Zhongqiu, Ye Jinqiu, Xu Shuiren, Ye Bingren, and more than ten others to provide free consultations, dispense medicine, and administer vaccinations. It is reported that all preparatory procedures have been completed, and the opening is scheduled for the 25th of this month, truly a savior for the poor and sick in western Shanghai.

Qingxu Temple Holds Memorial Service for Fallen Soldiers

Sixteen Days and Nights of Sutra Chanting

Qingxu Temple Taoist Temple at the intersection of Aiduya Road and Xizang Road, in light of the country's troubles, the people's poverty, and the continuous natural disasters, coupled with the enemy's invasion and killings, has decided to hold a grand sixteen-day and night memorial service from July 17th to August 1st to pray for the fallen soldiers and for the elimination of disasters and peace. The first day of the opening ceremony was the other day, and many devout men and women went to offer incense. It is reported that all expenses are borne by the temple itself and no donations are solicited externally. The temple is happy to receive and burn any donations of silver ingots.

Ship Industry Organizes Special Committee for Unified Weights and Measures

The matter of unified weights and measures has long been ordered by the municipal government to be implemented uniformly throughout the city. Now, the Puyi Fishing Boat Association, the Zhejiang Eastern Salt Boat Office, and the Fourth District Transportation Workers' Union have requested the Shanghai Boating and Shipping Industry Association to organize a special committee to be responsible for handling the matter of unified weights and measures. The executive committee of the Shipping Industry Association has approved the organization of a joint effort by various associations to proceed uniformly, and has designated Ma Weizhongxiang as the convener. The association convened its first meeting yesterday, with the participation of committee members Ye Liansheng, Lin Shicai, Xu Shouyue, Xu Jundao, Yao Shengzhu, Ma Ziliang, Shi Longsheng, Qiu Huanjia, Chen Ruiqing, Ma Zhongxiang, and others. After discussion, the following resolutions were made: (1) To determine the list of committee members. It was resolved that, in addition to the representatives of the aforementioned four groups as ex officio members, new members must be introduced by two committee members and must be relevant to the industry before being admitted. (2) To designate Comrade Ma Zhongxiang as the chairman. (3) The internal organization will be divided into four sections: finance, investigation, documentation, and public relations, to be undertaken by the aforementioned four groups. The meeting address will be temporarily located inside the Puyi Association in Yongheli, Wusong Road. The office will begin operations immediately. The association will report to the Shipping Industry Association and request the Party and government authorities for filing and registration, and will set August 1 as the date for implementation.

Publication of New Life Elementary School Textbooks

In order to promote education and cultivate national talents, Datong Bookstore is actively editing New Life Elementary School textbooks while successively publishing middle school textbooks. However, this matter is of great importance and progress is quite difficult. No aspect of writing, compilation, proofreading, or printing can be taken lightly. After a year of effort and struggle, fortunately, each book can be published successively before the autumn school opening, including five types: Chinese, arithmetic, social studies, nature, and art. The editors are all members of the curriculum development committee, and are editing according to the latest curriculum standards. The materials used are purely centered on the actual lives of children, and focus on adapting to new environments. The method of writing teaching practices is also different from the usual teaching books. Although teachers have different experiences and children have different abilities, they can feel the natural interest of teaching activities by using the various methods described in the teaching practices. It is truly a complete set of elementary school textbooks before the new curriculum standards are promulgated, and stands at the forefront of the times, worthy of being called "New Life."

Machine-Made Felt Hat Factories Prevent Inferior Goods from Being Mixed In and Passing Off

The Shanghai Felt Hat Industry Association and its members, machine-made felt hat manufacturers throughout the city, are aware that recently there have been unscrupulous merchants who, for petty profits, either falsely use the names of foreign merchants, mix and sell inferior felt hats, or alter imported inferior felt hats by adding trademarks and brand names to pass them off as domestic goods, confusing the genuine with the fake. This not only destroys commercial ethics, but also affects the future of domestic goods. Therefore, sixteen felt hat manufacturers have carefully devised prevention measures, publishing the trademarks and brand names of the sixteen companies in newspapers, and submitting them to Party and government agencies and various organizations for verification and filing. In the future, if any mixing occurs, once discovered, they will be investigated according to the law.

Letter

To the Editor: Regarding the news item in yesterday's newspaper about the temporary closure of the San You Society's retail department, it was stated that "the factory notified the power company to remove the current meter," which is not in accordance with the facts. It was found that the power company received a notification from the factory that day to go and remove important components of the power generating motor, which caused panic among all the workers and led to them automatically going to the company to petition. Also, when the petition was made on the 16th, because the workers were mostly orderly, the retail department did not close its iron doors. We hereby request a correction. Thank you for your attention. Sincerely, Shanghai Seventh District Cotton Textile Workers Union, July 18.

Letter

A Fair Discussion on the Issue of Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan Currency by Wu Jingxiong

The proposal to abolish taels and change to yuan currency has been advocated for a long time. When the National Currency Regulations were promulgated in the third year of the Republic of China, the government had the determination to unify the currency system. Subsequently, through the suggestions of the financial community and the advocacy of well-known scholars, more than ten years have passed. The reason for the delay in achieving this can be stated as follows: (1) Politics have not been brought on track. Abolishing taels and changing to yuan currency is not simply an economic issue. The political components it contains are even greater. Because politics cannot be brought on track, provinces govern themselves, and the central government has no power to refute them. Once taels are abolished and changed to yuan currency, it will create an opportunity for the provinces to seek profits. This is one reason. The power of judgment has not been recovered. Foreign banks use unequal treaties as shields, issuing paper money and absorbing deposits in various ports of our country. Once implemented, it will be like frightening birds in the forest. This is the second reason. There is no large-scale mint that can use accurate fineness to supply sufficient new coins to meet the needs of the whole country, while also giving people the opportunity to freely mint. This is the third reason. Domestic banks are numerous and paper money is rampant. Once taels are abolished and changed to yuan currency, the circulation of paper money will inevitably become wider. If there is a disturbance, the mistakes of the Pinghan Railway in the past are worrisome. Before the political situation is stable and the issuance system is comprehensively reorganized, once implemented, counterfeit currencies will emerge in large numbers. This is the fourth reason. Other details are too numerous to mention. In recent years, only the Shanghai Mint has been built on the banks of the Suzhou River, with a large scale, capable of minting one million yuan day and night. If the fineness can be unified and the management is strict, then the third point can be avoided. This is the only achievement of advocating abolishing taels and changing to yuan currency for more than ten years. What is the progress of the other three points compared to the past? Have the obstacles that hindered progress in the past been completely removed? This is what we should carefully consider before implementing the abolition of taels and changing to yuan currency.

The harm of using both taels and yuan is known to everyone and can be spoken of by everyone. The benefits of abolishing taels and changing to yuan currency, and the urgency of abolishing taels and changing to yuan currency, are also known to everyone and can be spoken of by everyone. What need is there to repeat them? What I want to say now is, in the current environment, even if the abolition of taels and changing to yuan currency is achieved as desired, will the benefits obtained outweigh the harm suffered? Forcing seedlings to grow is what people of the past warned against. Can what we are doing now avoid the criticism of forcing seedlings to grow? I sincerely hope that people from all walks of life will calmly discuss it. Don't those who advocate abolishing taels and changing to yuan currency immediately say that the price of customs taels is falling daily and the market is deteriorating daily, and that abolishing taels and changing to yuan currency will revitalize trade and benefit people's livelihood? If so, then Britain, the United States, and Japan are all countries with excellent currency systems. The United States is famous for its wealth in the world, and its gold standard stands firm. Why is the recession also spreading throughout the country? Economic recession has complex causes. As far as our country is concerned, the decline of the rural areas, the plight of the people, the prevalence of natural and man-made disasters, and the entanglement of internal strife and external insults all contribute to it, but they cannot be remedied by abolishing taels and changing to yuan currency. Some say that recently, countries are advocating expanding credit and inflating currency as the only prescription for treating the recession, such as the Bank of England repeatedly reducing interest rates and increasing loans, and powerful parties in the United States strongly advocating minting silver coins and issuing unprepared paper money. The purpose is to inflate the currency so that prices can rise, people's purchasing power can be increased, and production and sales can be matched, and then the economy can gradually return to its original state. Now, if our country abolishes taels and changes to yuan currency, the circulation of silver yuan will become wider and the issuance of paper money will become more. Chips will be rampant and currency inflation will lead to the same goal as the economic relief plans of various countries through different routes. The answer is that this is not understanding our country's relief organization. Today, China's position is inversely proportional to that of countries using the gold standard. It does not suffer from overproduction, but from too little. It does not suffer from falling prices, but from rising prices. Due to years of natural and man-made disasters, fields are barren and the price of gold is extremely high. Prices of all goods are soaring. After the January 28 Incident, the wounds are all over and vitality is lost. To recuperate, the first priority is to reduce the currency, not to expand the currency, and to lower prices, not to raise prices. Therefore, the economic relief plans of various countries will become a suicidal policy in our country. Those who imitate me die. How can things in the world be easily imitated? Recently, Jiang Jun published an article in Shen Bao (see Shen Bao on July 11 and 12) entitled "What Are We Waiting For to Abolish Taels and Change to Yuan Currency?" He believes that the current concerns about the expansion of paper currency after the abolition of taels and changing to yuan currency are untenable. He cites the issuance amount of various banks in Shanghai and the warehouse receipts as proof, believing that the current issuance preparations for general paper money are sufficient and there is no fear of price drops. Regarding this point, we believe that it should be studied as two questions. Is it necessary to inflate the currency at the moment? Is the result of abolishing taels and changing to yuan currency helping to inflate the currency as a problem? After the currency is inflated, how will the paper money preparation be regulated? Is the current 46 preparation system and the public inspection method of each issuing bank considered perfect and impeccable? Does the government have the power to control national issuance? Can we avoid repeating the mistakes of the Pinghan Railway in the past as another problem? At present, the ready cash in the mainland is useless and is concentrated in the commercial center. Tianjin, Shanghai, Pinghan all feel the pain of excess chips. High prices are caused by this. Therefore, the currency needs to be reduced urgently and should not be inflated, which is an obvious fact. If we rashly abolish taels and change to yuan currency at this time, the mint will inevitably actively mint new coins to comply with the law. At the same time, once silver taels lose their currency effect everywhere, they will inevitably be sent to the mint to be recast into silver yuan. The number of silver yuan will naturally increase day by day, and people will compete for paper money due to the inconvenience of using cash. Therefore, issuing banks (including foreign banks) will inevitably take the opportunity to actively expand the issuance amount to meet the needs, and the inflation of currency will be unstoppable. The unmanageable situation of Feng banknotes and the sudden rise and fall of Guangdong banknotes are obvious to everyone. As for the Pinghan incident in the past, people still change color when talking about it. It was found that the preparations of various banks in Hankou at that time were all handled according to the law, but they were difficult to resist due to environmental forces, and they finally became a situation of suspension of exchange. The severity of the situation at that time cannot be forgotten. If an incident happens again in the future, if we unfortunately repeat the mistakes of the Pinghan Railway, the harm will be a hundred times greater than in the past. Before its number is greater and the area of circulation is wider. Therefore, before the political situation is clear and the issuance power has not been unified, if measures are taken carelessly, it will cause endless disasters to the society. It is unacceptable to give up eating because of choking, but how can it be wise to knowingly commit a crime? It is necessary to consider this carefully.

Furthermore, from the perspective of the fineness of silver coins, the current types are complex and the fineness varies. Even with the new coins of President Yuan, the fineness is uneven. To abolish taels and change to yuan currency, it is necessary to concentrate minting, strictly stipulate the fineness of new coins, diligently add chemical verification, and properly supervise them. Without making the fineness vary, the credit of the new coins can be established. Give people the opportunity to freely mint, so that the use of new coins can be unimpeded far and wide. Some say that the Shanghai Mint is already doing this well. Why worry about it? I don't know that this requires a strong central government, with orders being carried out, making the provinces and regions submit and dare not hold different opinions. Otherwise, the power to mint coins still cannot be concentrated. Following the example of provinces governing themselves, those who abused the minting of copper coins in the past will go on to abuse the minting of silver yuan and use them in the market. The result is unbearable to say. Our suggestion is made with caution for this reason.

When people discuss abolishing taels and changing to yuan currency, they must criticize silver taels without reservation. Throwing stones at someone who has fallen into a well is a common technique of the Chinese people. I do not want to make a false statement. Think about it. Over the past few decades, there have been many major calamities, and there have been frequent disturbances in the market. However, the panic has finally subsided, and the market has finally avoided collapse. It is not that it has implicitly received the benefit of double preparation under the parallel use of taels and yuan. Because of Chinese and foreign trade, large and small contracts, claims and debts are mostly based on silver taels, although the fineness of silver yuan has been high and low over the years, and there have been ups and downs in paper money, prices have been stabilized a lot invisibly. We see that the result of the provinces' abuse of minting copper coins has led to a sharp drop in the price of copper coins. As a result, the prices of daily necessities valued in copper coins have risen sharply. The poor people whose income is based on copper coins are greatly affected by the difficulty of making a living. Although their income can also be required to increase, the speed of its increase can never be as fast as the rise in prices. Therefore, the pain suffered in a certain period is difficult to describe. Fortunately, most people in society are not affected because their income is in silver yuan, and silver yuan is backed by silver taels. Now, if taels are abolished and changed to yuan currency, the silver taels whose actual value is equal to the face value will disappear. If there are problems with the fineness of silver coins and the preparation of paper money, all kinds of goods valued in silver yuan will inevitably skyrocket in order to make up for the loss. At that time, the commotion caused in the entire society will be unbearable, and the economic organization will collapse and inundate the people in deep water and fire. Therefore, should it not be considered carefully before implementation? (To be continued)

The Entire Finnish Team Will Withdraw from the Competition

Helsinki, 17th (Xinhua News Agency) The sports community here, upon hearing that the president of the International Amateur Athletic Federation, Estes Delomo, declared in New York that Finnish long-distance running star Nurmi is still not considered qualified, is indignant and solemnly declares that if Nurmi is not allowed to participate in the World Games, the entire Finnish team will withdraw from the competition.
